2:27:1591:0:14:72:409:700:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Limits to Arbitrage and Hedging: Evidence from Commodity Markets
2:28:1655:14:14:72:359:686:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Viral V. Acharya, Lars A. Lochstoer, and Tarun Ramadorai
2:29:1711:14:14:72:234:672:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:NBER Working Paper No. 16875
2:30:1739:14:14:72:130:658:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:March 2011
2:31:1749:14:28:72:207:644:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:JEL No. G12,G13,G24,G33
2:32:1772:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:?:ABSTRACT
2:33:1780:28:14:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Motivated by the literature on limits-to-arbitrage, we build an equilibrium model of commodity markets
2:34:1882:14:14:72:540:574:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:in which speculators are capital constrained, and commodity producers have hedging demands for
2:35:1976:14:14:72:540:560:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:commodity futures. Increases (decreases) in producers' hedging demand (speculators' risk-capacity)
2:36:2074:14:14:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:increase hedging costs via price-pressure on futures, reduce producers' inventory holdings, and thus
2:37:2174:14:14:72:540:532:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:spot prices. Consistent with our model, producers' default risk forecasts futures returns, spot prices,
2:38:2277:14:14:72:540:518:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:and inventories in oil and gas market data from 1980-2006, and the component of the commodity 
2:39:2371:14:14:72:540:504:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:futures risk premium associated with producer hedging demand rises when speculative activity reduces.
2:40:2472:14:14:72:540:490:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:We conclude that limits to financial arbitrage generate limits to hedging by producers, and affect both
2:41:2575:14:42:72:182:476:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:asset and goods prices.
2:42:2598:42:14:72:155:434:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Viral V. Acharya
2:43:2614:14:14:72:192:420:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Stern School of Business
2:44:2638:14:14:72:176:406:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:New York University
2:45:2657:14:14:72:217:392:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:44 West 4th Street, Suite 9-84
2:46:2687:14:14:72:179:378:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:New York, NY 10012
2:47:2705:14:14:72:124:364:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:and NBER
2:48:2713:14:28:72:191:350:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:vacharya@stern.nyu.edu
2:49:2735:28:14:72:159:322:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Lars A. Lochstoer
2:50:2752:14:14:72:201:308:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Columbia Business School
2:51:2776:14:14:72:259:294:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Department of Economics and Finance

2:59:2908:14:14:306:407:406:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:University of Oxford
2:60:2928:14:14:306:363:392:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:Park End St
2:61:2939:14:14:306:478:378:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:Oxford OX1 1HP, United Kingdom
2:62:2969:14:0:306:452:364:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:tarun.ramadorai@sbs.ox.ac.uk
3:63:2997:0:28:72:201:691:209:g_d0_f2:209:g_d0_f2:C:1Introduction
3:64:3010:28:16:72:539:663:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:The neoclassical theory of asset pricing (Debreu (1959)) has been confronted by theory and evidence
3:65:3109:16:17:72:539:647:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that highlight the numerous frictions faced byfinancial intermediaries in undertaking arbitrage
3:66:3204:17:16:72:539:630:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:(Shleifer and Vishny (1997)), and the consequent price effects of such frictions. These price effects
3:67:3305:16:16:71:539:614:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:appear to be amplified in situations in whichfinancial intermediaries are substantially on one side
3:68:3404:16:17:71:539:598:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of the market (say, for instance, when they bear the prepayment and default risk of households in
3:69:3501:17:16:71:539:581:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:mortgage markets, or when they provide catastrophe insurance to households, as in Froot (1999)).
3:70:3597:16:17:71:539:565:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:In this paper, we apply the “limits to arbitrage” view to the analysis of commodity futures markets,
3:71:3697:17:16:71:539:548:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:asignificant sector of the economy that has recently experienced significant asset price movements
3:72:3795:16:17:71:539:532:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:as well as a renewed surge of attention fromfinancial economists. In our theoretical model, com-
3:73:3891:17:16:71:539:515:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:modity investment funds — speculators — are are constrained in their ability to deploy capital in the
3:74:3992:16:16:71:539:499:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:commodity futures market, and meet demands for hedging that come from commodity producing
3:75:4081:16:17:71:539:483:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f3:B:firms. The model, as well as our empirical analysis,reveals that this limit to arbitrage translates
3:76:4180:17:16:71:539:466:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:into “limits to hedging” experienced by producers, which in turn impacts real variables such as the
3:77:4279:16:17:71:178:450:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:spot commodity price.
3:78:4300:17:16:88:539:433:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:More specifically, the limit on the risk-taking capacity of speculators implies a price impact of
3:79:4397:16:17:71:539:417:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the hedging demand of risk-averse producers, who are naturally short commodity futures. This price
3:80:4495:17:16:71:540:400:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:impact constitutes a cost of hedging, which has consequences for the optimal inventory holding of
3:81:4592:16:16:71:540:384:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:commodity producers, and in turn, the commodityspot price. We derive implications of producer
3:82:4685:16:17:71:539:368:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:risk aversion and speculator capital constraints for the absolute and relative levels of futures and
3:83:4785:17:16:71:540:351:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:spot prices. To understand the comparative statics generated by the model, consider the following
3:84:4882:16:17:71:539:335:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:example: assume that producers as a whole need to hedge more by shorting futures contracts,
3:85:4973:17:16:71:540:318:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:say, on account of their rising default risk. Given that speculators are limited in their ability to
3:86:5073:16:17:71:539:302:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:take positions to satisfy this demand, it depresses futures prices and makes hedging more expensive.
3:87:5173:17:16:71:539:285:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Consequently, producers scale back on holding inventory, releasing it into the market and depressing
3:88:5273:16:17:71:539:269:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:spot prices. Therefore, futures risk premia and expected percentage change in the spot price have
3:89:5370:17:16:71:539:252:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:a common driver — the hedging demand of producers.  Due to this common driver, the model
3:90:5458:16:16:71:539:236:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:also predicts that the commodity convenience yield (or basis) should not be strongly related to
3:91:5553:16:17:71:530:220:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:commodity futures risk premia. Increases in speculators’ capital constraints have similar effects.
3:92:5651:17:16:88:539:203:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:To test the implications of our model, we employ data on spot and futures prices for heating oil,
3:93:5748:16:17:71:539:187:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:crude oil, gasoline and natural gas over the period 1980 to 2006. To identify changes in producers’
3:94:5847:17:16:71:539:170:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:risk aversion and hedging demand, we use movements in the default risk of commodity producing
3:95:5940:16:16:71:538:154:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f3:B:firms, an identification strategy driven by extant theoretical and empirical work on hedging.1We
3:96:6036:16:15:84:539:138:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:1A large body of theoretical work and empirical evidence on hedging has attributed managerial aversion to risk
3:97:6146:15:11:72:539:123:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:as a primary motive for hedging byfirms (Amihud and Lev (1981), Tufano (1996), Acharya, Amihud and Litov
3:98:6250:11:11:71:540:112:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:(2007), and Gormley and Matsa (2008), among others); and has documented that top managers suffer significantly
3:99:6360:11:0:71:539:101:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:fromfiring and job relocation difficulties whenfirms default (Gilson (1989), Baird and Rasmussen (2006) and Ozelge
4:100:6475:0:17:72:539:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:employ three different aggregate measures of the default risk of oil and gas producers in our work:
4:101:6574:17:16:72:540:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:a balance-sheet based measure — the Zmijewski (1984) score; a measure that combines market data
4:102:6669:16:17:72:540:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:with balance-sheet data — the Moody’s KMV’s expected default frequency; and a pure market-based
4:103:6764:17:16:72:540:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:measure — the lagged three-year stock return of these producers. Ourfindings are as follows: First,
4:104:6863:16:17:72:540:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:commodity producer default risk is positively related to both aggregate and individual producer
4:105:6958:17:16:72:540:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hedging demand. The latter is measured using information from the FAS 133 disclosures in annual
4:106:7053:16:16:72:539:592:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and quarterly reports, while the former is measuredas the net short positions of market participants
4:107:7153:16:17:72:540:576:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:classified as ‘hedgers’ by the Commodity Futures Trading Commission (CFTC). Second, an increase
4:108:7248:17:16:72:540:559:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:in the default risk of producers forecasts an increase in the excess returns on short-term futures of
4:109:7349:16:17:72:539:543:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:these commodities. The effect is robust to business-cycle conditions and economically significant:
4:110:7447:17:16:72:539:526:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:a one standard deviation increase in the aggregate commodity sector default risk is on average
4:111:7541:16:17:72:539:510:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:associated with a 4% increase in the respective commodity’s quarterly futures risk premium.2Third,
4:112:7639:17:16:72:540:493:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the effect of the default risk of producers on futures risk premia is greater in periods with higher
4:113:7739:16:17:72:540:477:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:(conditional) volatility of commodity prices, consistent with such periods being associated with
4:114:7835:17:16:72:540:460:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:greater risk of commodity stock outs and a lower risk appetite in thefinancial intermediation sector.
4:115:7936:16:16:72:539:444:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Fourth, wefind that the fraction of the futures risk premium attributable toproducers’ default
4:116:8030:16:17:71:539:428:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:risk is higher in periods in which broker-dealer balance-sheets and the assets under management
4:117:8125:17:16:71:539:411:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of commodity-focused funds are shrinking (these two measures of speculator risk appetite also
4:118:8218:16:17:71:540:395:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:predict futures risk premia, consistent with our model). Finally, as producer default risk increases,
4:119:8319:17:16:71:539:378:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:our model predicts that producers will hold less inventory, depressing current spot prices. This
4:120:8415:16:17:71:540:362:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:prediction is also confirmed in the data — increases in the default risk of oil and gas producers
4:121:8512:17:16:71:326:345:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:predict both lower inventory and higher spot returns.
4:122:8565:16:16:88:539:329:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:We verify that our results are driven by changes in producer hedging demand in a number of
4:123:8655:16:17:71:539:313:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:ways. First, we employ a “matching” approach. In particular, we separate the sample of producers
4:124:8751:17:16:71:539:296:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:into thosefirms that hedge commodity price exposure using derivatives (identified by their FAS
4:125:8845:16:17:72:540:280:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:133 disclosures between 1998-2006), versus those that do not hedge. We show that our results are
4:126:8941:17:16:72:539:263:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:drivenonlyby measures of aggregate hedging demand derived from thefirms that hedge. Second,
4:127:9032:16:17:72:539:247:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:we account for the possibility that default risk of commodity producers may be related to business-
4:128:9131:17:16:72:539:230:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:cycle conditions that also drive risk premiums. In particular, we employ controls in our forecasting
4:129:9231:16:16:72:540:214:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:regressions, in the form of variables commonly employed to predict the equity premium, such as
4:130:9325:16:17:72:540:198:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:changes in forecasts of GDP growth, the risk-free rate, the term spread, and the aggregate default
4:131:9423:17:16:72:540:181:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:spread, and confirm that our results are unaffected by the introduction of these controls. Third,
4:132:9520:16:17:72:540:165:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:from the set of commodityfirms that are included in our Crude Oil measures, we separate out pure
4:133:9616:17:20:72:540:148:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:play refiners from those that extract (or extract and refine) the commodity. Since refiners use crude
4:134:9717:20:11:72:539:128:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:(2007)). Fehle and Tsyplakov (2005) argue, both theoretically and empirically, thatfirms hedge more actively when
4:135:9830:11:7:71:157:117:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:default risk is higher.
4:136:9853:7:0:84:537:110:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:2Futures risk premia are identified through standard forecasting regressions as in, e.g., Fama and French (1987).
5:137:9967:0:17:72:540:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:oil as an input, their hedging demand is likely to be in the opposite direction to that of producers
5:138:10067:17:16:72:539:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:—weverifythisdifferential effect in the data. Finally, we employ controls that are commodity
5:139:10159:16:17:71:540:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:specific, such as the basis, inventory, lagged futuresreturn, and the realized variance of futures
5:140:10257:17:16:71:539:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:returns in our specifications. This is to control for the possibility that producer default risk - an
5:141:10358:16:17:72:540:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:endogenous variable - may also be related to supply uncertainty, in the form of the likelihood of
5:142:10455:17:16:72:539:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:inventory stock-outs or other production shocks. Our model predicts that such supply uncertainty
5:143:10551:16:16:72:540:592:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:is related to the variance of the commodity price, but that increases in producer risk aversion
5:144:10646:16:17:72:539:576:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:should have effects as outlined earlier, even after controlling for this effect. The empirics confirm
5:145:10747:17:16:72:540:559:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that default risk, our proxy for producer risk aversion, continues to explain futures risk premia after
5:146:10850:16:17:72:540:543:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the introduction of these controls, indeed, there is an interactive effect of this predictive power with
5:147:10954:17:16:72:539:526:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:realized futures return variance as predicted bythe model. To summarize, our model implies that
5:148:11049:16:17:72:539:510:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:limits to arbitrage generate limits to hedging forfirms in the real economy. Consequently, factors
5:149:11147:17:16:72:539:493:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that capture time-variation in such limits have predictive power for asset prices and affect outcomes
5:150:11248:16:17:71:539:477:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:in underlying product markets (spot prices and inventories). Our empirical results are consistent
5:151:11345:17:16:71:487:460:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:with the implications of the model and robust to a number of alternative explanations.
5:152:11431:16:16:88:539:444:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The remainder of the introduction relates our paper to the literature.  Section 2 introduces
5:153:11523:16:17:71:539:428:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:our model. Section 3 presents our empirical strategy. Section 4 establishes the link between the
5:154:11619:17:16:71:539:411:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hedging demand of commodity producers and measures of their default risk at the individualfirm
5:155:11713:16:17:72:474:395:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:level. Section 5 discusses our main, aggregate empirical results. Section 6 concludes.
5:156:11799:17:16:88:540:378:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f3:A:Related Literature.There are two classic views on the behavior of commodity forward and
5:157:11886:16:17:72:540:362:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:futures prices. TheTheory of Normal Backwardation(Keynes (1930)), states that speculators, who
5:158:11980:17:16:72:540:345:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:take the long side of a commodity futures position, require a risk premium for hedging the spot price
5:159:12081:16:16:72:540:329:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:exposure of producers (an early version of the “limits to arbitrage” argument). The risk premium
5:160:12177:16:17:72:540:313:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:on long forward positions is thus increasing in the amount of demand pressure from hedgers and
5:161:12271:17:16:72:540:296:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:should be related to observed hedger and speculator positions in the commodity forward markets.
5:162:12366:16:17:72:540:280:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Carter, Rausser and Schmitz (1983), Chang (1985), Bessembinder (1992), and de Roon, Nijman,
5:163:12457:17:16:72:540:263:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and Veld (2000) empirically link this “hedging pressure” to futures excess returns, the basis and
5:164:12554:16:17:72:357:247:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the convenience yield, as evidence in support of this theory.
5:165:12615:17:16:88:540:230:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:TheTheory of Storage(Kaldor (1939), Working (1949), and Brennan (1958)), on the other
5:166:12700:16:16:72:540:214:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hand, postulates that forward prices are driven by optimal inventory management. In particular,
5:167:12795:16:17:72:539:198:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:this theory introduces the notion of aconvenience yieldto explain why anyone would hold inventory
5:168:12892:17:16:72:540:181:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:in periods in which spot prices are expected to decline.  Tests of the theory include Fama and
5:169:12986:16:17:72:540:165:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:French (1987) and Ng and Pirrong (1994). In more recent work, Routledge, Seppi and Spatt (2000)
5:170:13081:17:16:72:540:148:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:introduce a forward market into the optimal inventory management model of Deaton and Laroque
5:171:13173:16:17:72:540:132:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:(1992) and show that time-varying convenience yields, consistent with those observed in the data,
5:172:13270:17:16:72:325:115:121:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:B:can arise even in the presence of risk-neutral agents.3
5:173:13325:16:0:84:543:99:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:3There is a large literature on reduced form, no-arbitragemodelingofcommodityfuturesprices(e.g.,Brennan
6:174:13429:0:17:88:539:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The two theories are not mutually exclusive.  A time-varying risk premium on forwards is
6:175:13517:17:16:71:540:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:consistent with optimal inventory management if producers are not risk-neutral or face (say) bank-
6:176:13615:16:17:71:539:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:ruptcy costs; and speculator capital is not unlimited, as in our model. In the data, wefind that
6:177:13711:17:16:71:539:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hedgers are net short forwards on average, while speculators are net long, which indicates that
6:178:13806:16:17:71:539:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:producers do have hedging demands.  In support of this view, Haushalter (2000, 2001) surveys
6:179:13898:17:16:71:540:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:100 oil and gas producers over the 1992 to 1994 period andfinds that close to 50 percent of them
6:180:13994:16:16:71:539:592:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hedge, in the amount of approximately a quarter of their production each year. In a recent paper,
6:181:14091:16:17:71:540:576:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Gorton, Hayashi, and Rouwenhorst (2007) provide evidence that futuresrisk premia are related
6:182:14183:17:16:71:540:559:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:to inventory levels. Consistent with theirfindings, our model also predicts that inventory should
6:183:14280:16:17:71:540:543:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:forecast commodity futures returns. In our model, this results is driven by the interaction between
6:184:14379:17:16:71:539:526:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:capital-constrained speculators and producer hedging demand, proxied by measures of producer de-
6:185:14475:16:17:71:539:510:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:fault risk. Our empirical contribution is to identify that this default risk measure helps to explain
6:186:14576:17:16:71:508:493:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:commodity spot prices, risk premia, CFTC hedging pressure measures and inventory levels.
6:187:14664:16:17:88:539:477:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:In closely related work, Hirshleifer (1988, 1989, 1990) considers the interaction between hedgers
6:188:14761:17:16:71:539:460:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and arbitrageurs.  In particular, Hirshleifer(1990) observes that in equilibrium there must be
6:189:14855:16:16:71:539:444:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:a friction to investing in commodity futures in order for hedging demand to affect prices and
6:190:14948:16:17:71:539:428:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:quantities. In our model, this friction arises due to limited movement of capital, motivated by the
6:191:15047:17:16:71:539:411:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:‘limits to arbitrage’ literature, and hedging demand of producers, motivated by a principal-agent
6:192:15144:16:17:71:539:395:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:problem as the commodityfirm is ultimately owned by the consumers. Furthermore, our analysis,
6:193:15237:17:16:71:540:378:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:unlike Hirshleifer’s, is also empirical. As a usefulconsequence, in addition to providing evidence
6:194:15335:16:17:71:540:362:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:for our model, we are able to confirm many of the propositions of Hirshleifer’s (1988, 1989, 1990)
6:195:15433:17:16:71:540:345:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:theoretical models, using a different approach than that in Bessembinder (1992). Another related
6:196:15529:16:16:71:540:329:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:paper is by Bessembinder and Lemmon (2002), who show that hedging demand affects spot and
6:197:15618:16:17:71:539:313:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:futures prices in electricity markets when producers are risk averse. They highlight that the absence
6:198:15719:17:16:71:539:296:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of storage is what allows for predictable intertemporal variation in equilibrium prices. We show in
6:199:15818:16:17:71:539:280:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:this paper that the price impact can arise even in the presence of storage in the oil and gas markets.
6:200:15920:17:16:88:539:263:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, it has proven difficult to explain the unconditional risk premiums on commodity fu-
6:201:16012:16:17:71:539:247:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:tures using traditional asset pricing theory (see Jagannathan, (1985) for an earlier effort). Although
6:202:16114:17:16:71:539:230:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:conditional risk premiums on commodity futures do appear to be reliably non-zero (see Bessem-
6:203:16207:16:16:71:539:214:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:binder (1992)), Bessembinder and Chan (1992) document that the forecastability of price changes
6:204:16302:16:17:71:539:198:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:in commodity futures is based on different asset pricing factors as compared to equity markets.
6:205:16397:17:16:71:539:181:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Furthermore, in a recent paper, Tang and Xiong (2009) show that the correlation between com-
6:206:16489:16:17:71:539:165:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:modity and equity markets increases in the amount of speculator capitalflowing to commodity
6:207:16580:17:16:71:539:148:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:markets. These results are consistent with our assumption of time-varying market segmentation
6:208:16673:16:20:71:265:132:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:between equity and commodity markets.
6:209:16710:20:11:72:540:112:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:(1991), Schwartz (1997), Cassasus and Collin-Dufresne (2005)). General equilibrium models of commodity pricing
6:210:16820:11:0:72:388:101:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:include Cassasus, Collin-Dufresne, and Routledge (2009), and Johnson (2009).
7:211:16897:0:28:72:174:691:209:g_d0_f2:209:g_d0_f2:C:2  The Model
7:212:16909:28:16:72:540:663:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:We present a two-period model of commodity spot and futures price determination that includes
7:213:17002:16:17:72:540:647:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:optimal inventory management, as in Deaton and Laroque (1992), and hedging demand, similar
7:214:17092:17:16:72:540:630:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:to the models of Anderson and Danthine (1980, 1983) and Hirshleifer (1988, 1990).  There are
7:215:17184:16:16:72:540:614:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:three types of agents in the model: (1) consumers, whose demand for the spot commodity along
7:216:17276:16:17:72:539:598:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:with the equilibrium supply determine the commodity spot price; (2) commodity producers, who
7:217:17368:17:16:72:539:581:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:manage profits by optimally managing their inventory and by hedging with commodity futures;
7:218:17459:16:17:71:540:565:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and (3) speculators, whose demand for commodity futures, along with the futures hedging demand
7:219:17553:17:32:71:330:548:121:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:B:of producers, determine the commodity futures price.4
7:220:17606:32:23:72:371:516:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:2.1  Consumption, Production and the Spot Price
7:221:17653:23:35:72:382:493:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Let commodity consumers’ inverse demand function be given by:

7:229:17821:16:17:71:540:409:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:tion of other goods, andandare positive constants. This inverse demand function obtains if the

7:231:18013:16:16:71:540:376:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of substitution equal to.  In the Appendix, we argue that the main predictions of our model
7:232:18105:16:17:71:539:360:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:presented here are robust to a general equilibrium setting where this inverse demand function is
7:233:18201:17:16:71:540:343:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:derived endogenously. In the partial equilibrium setting considered here, however,represents
7:234:18295:16:17:72:540:327:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:an exogenous demand shock, which we assume is lognormally distributed with[ln]=and
7:235:18381:17:16:71:540:310:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f3:B:[ln]=2. This shock captures changes in demand arising from sources such as technological
7:236:18475:16:17:71:539:294:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:changes in the production of substitutes and complements for the commodity, weather conditions,
7:237:18570:17:16:71:387:277:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:or other shocks that are not explicitly accounted for in the model.
7:238:18637:16:16:88:539:261:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Let aggregate inventory and production be denotedand, respectively. Further, letbe
7:239:18724:16:17:71:539:245:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the cost of storage; that is, individual producers can storeunits of the commodity at−1yielding
7:240:18821:17:16:71:540:228:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f3:B:(1−)units at,where∈(01)The commodity spot price is determined by market clearing,
7:241:18908:16:17:71:543:212:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:which demands that incoming aggregate inventory and current production,+(1−)−1,equals
7:242:18998:17:16:71:327:195:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:current consumption and outgoing inventory,+.
7:243:19047:16:15:84:539:179:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:4We model consumers of the commodity as operating only in the spot market.  This is an abstraction, which
7:244:19152:15:10:71:539:164:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:does not correspond exactly with the evidence - for instance airlines have been known periodically to hedge their
7:245:19265:10:11:71:539:154:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:exposure to the price of jet fuel (by taking long positions in the futures market). In the empirical section, we show
7:246:19382:11:11:71:539:143:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:that our results are not affected by controlling for a measure of consumers’ hedging demand. Furthermore the CFTC
7:247:19495:11:11:71:540:132:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:data on hedger positions indicates that speculative capital (e.g., in hedge funds) has historically been allocated to
7:248:19612:11:11:71:539:121:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:long positions in commodity futures, indicating that the sign of net hedger demand for futures is consistent with our
7:249:19729:11:0:71:119:110:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:assumption.
8:250:19741:0:24:72:162:691:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:2.2  Producers

8:279:21188:16:17:71:539:260:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:spot price. As can be seen from Equation (3), managers use inventories to smooth demand shock. If,
8:280:21286:17:16:71:539:243:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:however, the current demand shock is sufficiently high, an inventory stock-out occurs (i.e.,0),
8:281:21383:16:16:71:540:227:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and current spot prices can rise above expected future spot prices. In such a circumstance,firms
8:282:21479:16:15:84:540:211:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:5Note that the production schedule,0and1, is assumed to be pre-determined. The implicit assumption, which
8:283:21586:15:7:72:523:196:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:creates a role for inventory management, is that it is prohibitively costly to change production in the short-run.
8:284:21700:7:15:84:539:189:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:6The literature on corporate hedging provides several justifications for this modeling choice. Hedging demand
8:285:21809:15:11:71:539:174:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:could result from managers being underdiversified, as in Amihud and Lev (1981) and Stulz (1984), or better informed
8:286:21924:11:11:71:539:163:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:about the risks faced by thefirm (Breeden and Viswanathan (1990), and DeMarzo and Duffie (1995)). Managers
8:287:22030:11:11:71:540:152:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:could also be averse to variance on account of private costs suffered upon distress, as documented by Gilson (1989) for
8:288:22149:11:11:71:540:141:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:example, or thefirm may face deadweight costs offinancial distress, as argued by Smith and Stulz (1985). Aversion
8:289:22262:11:7:71:540:130:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:to earnings volatility can also be generated from costs of externalfinancing as in Froot, Scharfstein, and Stein (1993).
8:290:22382:7:15:84:539:123:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:7The setup implicitly assumes that the equity-holders cannot write a complete contract with the managers, on
8:291:22490:15:0:71:342:108:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:account of (for instance) incentive reasons as in Holmstrom (1979).
9:292:22558:0:17:72:540:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:wish to have negative inventory, but cannot. Thus, aconvenience yield for holding the spot arises,
9:293:22656:17:16:71:539:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:as those who hold the spot in the event of a stock-out get to sell at a temporarily high price. This
9:294:22756:16:17:71:539:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:is theTheory of Storageaspect of our model.8Importantly, inventory is increasing in the amount
9:295:22850:17:16:72:540:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hedged in the futures market,. That is, hedging allows the producer to hold more inventory as it
9:296:22948:16:17:72:540:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:reduces the amount of earnings variance that the producer would otherwise be exposed to. Thus,
9:297:23042:17:16:72:380:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the futures market provides an important venue for risk sharing.
9:298:23106:16:33:88:539:592:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Thefirst order condition for the numberof futures contracts that the producer goes short is:
9:299:23200:33:0:216:320:559:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f12:?:∗=∗(1−)+1−
9:300:23215:0:15:323:390:566:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f9:?:[Λ(1−)]
9:301:23225:15:0:345:367:551:121:g_d0_f7:65:g_d0_f8:A:2
9:302:23230:0:34:392:540:559:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f3:A:(4)
9:303:23234:34:16:72:539:525:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Note that if the futures priceis such that[Λ(1−)] = 0, there are no gains or costs to equity
9:304:23330:16:17:71:540:509:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:holders of the manager’s hedging activity in terms of expected, risk adjusted profits. The producer
9:305:23429:17:16:71:540:492:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:will therefore simply minimize the variance of period1profits by hedging fully. In this case, the
9:306:23526:16:16:71:539:476:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:manager’s optimal hedging strategy is independent of the degree of managerial risk aversion. This
9:307:23623:16:17:71:447:460:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:is a familiar result that arises by no-arbitrage in frictionless complete markets.
9:308:23705:17:16:88:539:443:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:If, however, the futures price is lower than what is considered fair from the equity-holders’
9:309:23798:16:17:71:539:427:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:perspective (i.e.,[Λ(1−)]0), it is optimal for the producer to increase the expected profits
9:310:23894:17:16:71:539:410:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:by entering a longspeculativefutures position after having fully hedged the period1supply. In
9:311:23987:16:17:71:539:394:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:other words, in this situation, the hedge is costly due to perceived mispricing in the commodity
9:312:24083:17:16:71:539:377:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:market, and it is no longer optimal to hedge the period1price exposure fully. This entails shorting
9:313:24182:16:16:71:539:361:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:fewer futures contracts.  Note that an increase in the manager’s risk aversiondecreases this
9:314:24276:16:32:71:312:345:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:implicit speculative futures position, all else equal.

9:331:24548:31:17:71:539:172:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:The convenience yield can only differ from zero if the shadow price of the inventory constraint ()
9:332:24647:17:16:71:539:155:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:is positive. In this case, the expected future spot price is low relative to the current spot price, and
9:333:24751:16:16:71:452:139:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:this results in the futures price also being low relative to the current spot price.
9:334:24835:16:15:84:539:123:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:8In a multi-period setting, a convenience yield of holding the spot arises in these models even if there is no actual
9:335:24952:15:0:71:518:108:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:stock-out,butaslongasthereisapositiveprobabilityof a stock-out (see Routledge, Seppi, and Spatt (2000)).
10:336:25057:0:17:88:539:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The basis is not a good measure of the futures risk premium when inventories are positive.
10:337:25147:17:16:71:539:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Producers in the model can obtain exposure to future commodity prices in one of two ways — either
10:338:25244:16:17:71:539:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:by going long a futures contract, or by holding inventory. In equilibrium, the marginal payofffrom
10:339:25342:17:16:71:539:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:these strategies must coincide. Thus, producers managing inventory enforce a common component
10:340:25435:16:17:71:539:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:in the payoffto holding the spot and holding the futures, with offsetting impacts on the basis. This
10:341:25535:17:16:71:539:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:prediction of the model is borne out in our empirical results, and is consistent with thefindings of
10:342:25635:16:32:71:191:592:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Fama and French (1987).
10:343:25658:32:24:72:170:560:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:2.3  Speculators
10:344:25674:24:16:72:539:536:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Speculators take the long positions that offset producers’ naturally short positions, and allow the
10:345:25773:16:17:71:540:520:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:market to clear. We assume that these speculators are specialized investment management com-
10:346:25865:17:16:71:539:503:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:panies, with superior investment ability in the commodity futures market (e.g., commodity hedge
10:347:25960:16:16:71:540:487:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:funds and investment bank commodity trading desks). As a consequence of this superior invest-
10:348:26053:16:17:71:540:471:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:ment technology, investors in otherfinancial assets (the equity-holders) only invest in commodity
10:349:26150:17:16:71:539:454:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:markets by delegating their investments to these specialized funds. As in Berk and Green (2004),
10:350:26246:16:17:71:539:438:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the managers of these funds extract all the surplus ofthis activity and the outside investors only get
10:351:26348:17:16:71:540:421:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:theirfairriskcompensation.Thepayoffto the fund manager per long futures contract is therefore
10:352:26441:16:17:71:539:405:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f3:B:[Λ(1−)], making the net present value for equity-holders of investing in a commodity fund
10:353:26533:17:16:71:229:388:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:zero, as dictated by no-arbitrage.
10:354:26567:16:17:88:540:372:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The commodity fund managers are assumed to be risk-neutral, but they are subject to capital
10:355:26658:17:16:71:540:355:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:constraints. These constraintscould arise from costs of leverage such as margin requirements, as
10:356:26754:16:16:71:539:339:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:well as from value-at-risk (VaR) limits. We model these capital constraints as proportional to the
10:357:26852:16:17:71:539:323:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:variance of the fund’s position, in the spirit of a VaR constraint, as in Danielsson, Shin, and Zigrand
10:358:26955:17:16:71:539:306:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:(2008).9Commodity funds are assumed to behave competitively, and we assume the existence of a
10:359:27048:16:30:71:280:290:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:representative fund with objective function:
10:360:27092:30:7:198:218:260:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f9:?:max

11:434:29842:16:0:71:540:131:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:risk aversion, and, speculator risk aversion. Note that Equation (11)holdsforanyconsumer
12:435:29933:0:32:72:269:691:121:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:B:preferences (inverse demand functions).10
12:436:29974:32:17:88:540:659:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f3:A:Comparative Statics.We are interested in comparative statics with respect to producers’

12:438:30154:16:16:71:540:626:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and the degree of the capital constraint on speculators,. The proof of the following Proposition
12:439:30252:16:29:71:539:610:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:is relegated to the Appendix, and we only give the economic intuition for the results in this section.

12:453:30635:16:16:88:539:479:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f6:A:The futures risk premium and the expected spot price return are increasing in the severity of
12:454:30728:16:25:71:237:463:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f6:C:speculators’ capital constraints,:
12:455:30764:25:15:198:204:438:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f7:C:

12:457:30768:0:15:211:261:438:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f9:A:[1−]

12:459:30776:0:0:265:311:431:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f6:C:0and
12:460:30781:0:15:329:335:438:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f7:C:
12:461:30782:15:0:324:339:423:121:g_d0_f7:65:g_d0_f8:?:
12:462:30785:0:15:342:395:438:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f9:A:[1−0]
12:463:30793:15:0:363:374:423:121:g_d0_f7:65:g_d0_f11:?:0
12:464:30795:0:36:399:539:431:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f3:A:0(13)
12:465:30802:36:16:71:534:395:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f6:C:where the latter only holds if there is not a stock-out. In the case of a stock-out,[1−0]0=0.
12:466:30903:16:17:88:539:379:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f6:A:The optimal inventory is decreasing in both producer and speculator hedging demand,  unless
12:467:30994:17:28:71:165:362:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f6:C:there is a stock-out.
12:468:31015:28:16:88:539:334:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The intuition for these results is as follows. When producers’ fundamental hedging demand ()
12:469:31109:16:17:71:540:318:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:increases, the manager’s sensitivity to the risk of holding unhedged inventory increases. In response
12:470:31210:17:16:71:539:301:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:to this, the manager reduces inventory and increases the proportion of future supply that is hedged.
12:471:31310:16:17:71:539:285:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:The former means that more of the commodity is sold on the spot market, which depresses current
12:472:31405:17:16:71:540:268:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:spot prices and raises future spot prices. The latter leads to a higher variance-adjusted demand
12:473:31501:16:17:71:539:252:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:for short futures contracts, which is accommodated by increasing the futures risk premium. An
12:474:31594:17:16:71:539:235:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:increase in speculator capital constraints,,hassimilareffect. The cost of hedging now increases
12:475:31691:16:16:71:539:219:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:as the speculators require a higher compensation per unit of risk. The direct effect of this is to
12:476:31789:16:16:71:540:203:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:decrease the number of short futures positions. However, this leaves the producer more exposed to
12:477:31886:16:15:80:539:187:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:10Since producer hedging demand and limits to arbitrage both affect the optimal supply (inventory) of the com-
12:478:31996:15:11:71:539:172:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:modity, the volatility of futures returns is also affected, meaning that the frictions assumed in the commodity market
12:479:32114:11:11:71:539:161:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:also show up in the standard risk adjustment (the covariance term). Thus, there is a component of the futures risk
12:480:32228:11:11:71:539:150:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:premium that originates from limits to arbitrage and hedging demand that cannot be separately observed from the
12:481:32339:11:11:71:539:139:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:standard risk adjustment. Symmetrically, if the volatility and mean of the demand shocks change, this is reflected
12:482:32453:11:11:71:539:128:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:in the volatility of the futures return which also shows up in the futures risk premium term due to hedging demand
12:483:32567:11:11:71:539:117:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:and limits to arbitrage. In the Appendix, we further discuss the interaction between the frictions proposed here and
12:484:32683:11:11:71:539:106:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:the standard risk adjustment in the context of a general equilibrium model where the pricing kernel and the inverse
12:485:32798:11:0:71:245:95:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:demand function are derived endogenously.
13:486:32841:0:17:72:539:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:period1spot price risk, and to mitigate this effect, optimal inventory also decreases. In a stock-out,
13:487:32943:17:16:71:539:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the inventory is constant (at zero) and consequently so are the expected spot price and its variance.
13:488:33044:16:17:71:539:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:In that case, the only effect of an increase in producer (or speculator) risk aversion is the direct
13:489:33144:17:16:71:439:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:effect on the futures risk premium, as the marginal cost of hedging increases.
13:490:33222:16:17:88:540:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:To evaluate the likely magnitudes of the effect of the model’s frictions and to illustrate the
13:491:33316:17:16:71:539:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:model results, we calibrate the model using key moments of the data: in particular, the volatility
13:492:33414:16:16:71:539:592:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of the commodity futures returns, commodity expenditure relative to aggregate endowment (GDP)
13:493:33507:16:17:71:539:576:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and aggregate endowment growth, as well as the mean and volatility of the equity market pricing
13:494:33602:17:16:71:378:559:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:kernel. The details of the calibration are given in the Appendix.
13:495:33667:16:17:88:539:543:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The severity of the model’s frictions are increasing in the variance aversion of producers and
13:496:33761:17:16:71:539:526:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:speculators,and. The variation in these quantities is shown in the two top graphs of Figure
13:497:33856:16:17:72:539:510:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f3:B:1as the producers’ cost of hedging and the Sharpe ratio earned by speculators, whereis on
13:498:33947:17:16:72:539:493:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the horizontal axis andis shown as a dashed line for high speculator risk aversion and a solid
13:499:34043:16:17:72:539:477:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:line for low speculator risk aversion. The remainder of the plots in Figure1shows that the spot
13:500:34138:17:16:72:539:460:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and futures risk premiums are indeed increasing in producer and speculator risk aversion, while
13:501:34233:16:16:72:545:444:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:inventory is decreasing.  The calibration implies economically significantvariationinbothspot
13:502:34326:16:17:72:540:428:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and futures risk premiums. In particular, for high speculator risk aversion (corresponding to their
13:503:34425:17:16:72:540:411:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:earning a quarterly Sharpe ratio of about025) and high hedging demand (corresponding to a loss
13:504:34520:16:17:72:539:395:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of about08%offirm value due to hedging), the abnormal quarterly futures risk premium is about
13:505:34614:17:16:72:539:378:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f3:B:6%, whereas for low producer hedging demand and speculator risk aversion (Sharpe ratio of about
13:506:34709:16:17:72:539:362:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f3:B:005and loss from hedging of about01%offirm value), the abnormal futures risk premium is less
13:507:34803:17:16:72:540:345:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:than1%. At the same time, the impact on inventory is about a1%to9%change in the level. The
13:508:34893:16:16:72:540:329:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:effect on expected percentage spot price changes is about the same as for the futures, since the cost
13:509:34994:16:17:72:540:313:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of carry relation holds when there is no stock-out. In sum, reasonable levels of the costs of hedging
13:510:35095:17:16:72:539:296:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and required risk compensation leads to economically significant abnormal returns in the futures
13:511:35191:16:17:72:372:280:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:market, and concomitant changes in inventory and spot prices.
13:512:35252:17:16:88:539:263:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Figure1also illustrates an intuitive interaction between speculator risk tolerance and producer
13:513:35347:16:17:72:539:247:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hedging demand. In particular, the response ofthe abnormal futures risk premium to changes in
13:514:35440:17:16:72:540:230:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:producer hedging demand is smaller when speculator risk tolerance is high. These are times when
13:515:35535:16:16:72:540:214:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:speculators are willing to meet the hedging demand of producers with small price concessions. If,
13:516:35632:16:17:72:539:198:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:conversely, speculators are more risk averse, the price concession required to meet an additional
13:517:35729:17:38:72:224:181:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:unit of hedging demand is high.
13:518:35760:38:27:72:230:143:209:g_d0_f2:209:g_d0_f2:C:3  Empirical Strategy
13:519:35781:27:17:72:539:116:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:In our empirical analysis we test the main predictions of the model, as laid out in Proposition1.
13:520:35878:17:0:71:540:99:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:To do so, we need proxies forand- the fundamental hedging demand and risk appetite of
14:521:35969:0:17:72:539:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:producers and speculators, respectively. Clearly, from Equation (11), to identify time-variation in
14:522:36068:17:16:72:540:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the futures risk premium from hedging pressure and limits to speculative capital, we must control for
14:523:36169:16:17:72:540:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the covariance of the futures return with the equity pricing kernel. We therefore apply a substantial
14:524:36270:17:16:72:540:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:set of controls and robustness checks in the empirical analysis in order to establish that ourfindings
14:525:36372:16:32:72:433:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:arise on account of producer hedging demand and limited arbitrage capital.
14:526:36446:32:24:72:277:593:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:3.1  Commodity Producer Sample
14:527:36476:24:16:72:539:569:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:To construct proxies for fundamental producerhedging demand, we employ data on commodity
14:528:36564:16:17:72:539:553:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:producingfirms’ accounting and stock returns from the CRSP-Compustat database. The use of
14:529:36653:17:16:72:540:536:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Compustat data limits the study to the oil and gas markets as these are the only commodity
14:530:36743:16:17:72:539:520:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:markets where there is a large enough set of producerfirms to create a reliable time-series of
14:531:36837:17:16:72:540:503:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:aggregate commodity sector producer hedging demand.  Our empirical analysis thus focuses on
14:532:36928:16:16:72:539:487:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:four commodities: crude oil, heating oil, gasoline, and natural gas. The full sample of producers
14:533:37025:16:17:72:539:471:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:includes allfirms with SIC codes 1310 and 1311 (Petroleum Refiners) and 2910 and 2911 (Crude
14:534:37117:17:16:72:539:454:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Petroleum and Gas Extraction).11The total sample of producers consists of 525firms with quarterly
14:535:37214:16:17:71:540:438:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:data going back to 1974 for somefirms. We also use data onfirms’ explicitly disclosed hedging
14:536:37307:17:32:71:508:421:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:activities from accounting statements available in the EDGAR database from 1998 to 2006.
14:537:37395:32:29:72:364:389:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:3.2  Proxying for Fundamental Hedging Demand
14:538:37439:29:17:99:512:360:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f6:C:“The amount of production we hedge is driven by the amount of debt on our consolidated
14:539:37525:17:21:99:428:343:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f3:C:balance sheet and the level of capital commitments we have in place.”
14:540:37594:21:28:99:409:322:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:C:- St. Mary Land & Exploration Co. in their 10-Kfiling for 2006.
14:541:37657:28:17:88:539:294:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:In the model, we refer to the variance aversion of the producers,, as producers’ fundamental
14:542:37751:17:16:72:539:277:121:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f8:B:hedging demand. In the empirical analysis, we propose that variation in the aggregate level of
14:543:37847:16:16:72:540:261:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:can be proxied for, using measures of aggregate default risk for the producers of the commodity.
14:544:37943:16:17:72:540:245:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:There are both empirical and theoretical motivations for this choice, which we discuss below. In
14:545:38039:17:16:72:539:228:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:addition, we show in the following section that the available micro-evidence of individual producer
14:546:38138:16:17:72:349:212:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hedging behavior in our sample supports this assumption.
14:547:38194:17:16:88:539:195:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The driver of hedging demand that we focus on is managerial aversion to distress and default.
14:548:38287:16:17:72:540:179:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:In particular, we postulate that managers act in an increasingly risk averse manner as the likelihood
14:549:38388:17:16:72:540:162:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of distress and default increases. Amihud and Lev (1981) and Stulz (1984) propose general aversion
14:550:38486:16:16:72:539:146:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of managers to variance of cashflows as a driver of hedging demand, the rationale being that while
14:551:38584:16:15:80:539:130:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:11These SIC classifications, however, are rather coarse:firmsdesignatedas“PetroleumRefiners” (e.g., Exxon)
14:552:38690:15:11:71:539:115:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:often also engage in extraction, and vice versa. In our robustness checks below, we separate out pure play refiners
14:553:38805:11:11:71:539:104:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:(as identified from their annual statements) fromfirms that engage in production, and separately evaluate the effects
14:554:38922:11:0:71:276:93:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:of default risk measures from each of these groups.
15:555:38975:0:17:72:539:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:shareholders can diversify acrossfirms in capital markets, managers are significantly exposed to their
15:556:39077:17:16:72:544:674:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f3:B:firms’ cash-flow risk due to incentive compensation as well as investments infirm-specifichuman
15:557:39172:16:17:72:540:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:capital. Empirical evidence has demonstratedthat managerial turnover is indeed higher infirms
15:558:39265:17:16:72:540:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:with higher leverage and deteriorating performance: e.g., Coughlan and Schmidt (1985), Warner
15:559:39358:16:17:72:540:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:et al. (1988) and Weisbach (1988) provide evidence that top management turnover is predicted
15:560:39450:17:16:72:540:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:by declining stock market performance. Gilson (1989) refines this evidence, and examines the role
15:561:39547:16:16:72:539:592:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of defaults and leverage. Hefirstfinds that management turnover is more likely following poor
15:562:39640:16:17:72:539:576:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:stock-market performance, and thatfirms that are highly leveraged or in default on their debt
15:563:39733:17:16:72:540:559:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:experience higher top management turnover than their counterparts. Gilson further documents
15:564:39824:16:17:72:539:543:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that following their resignation fromfirms in default, managers are not subsequently employed
15:565:39917:17:16:72:539:526:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:by another exchange-listedfirm for at least three years - consistent with managers experiencing
15:566:40012:16:17:72:540:510:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:large personal costs when theirfirms default. Finally, Haushalter (2000, 2001) in a survey of one
15:567:40109:17:16:72:539:493:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hundred oil and gasfirms over the 1992 to 1994 period, uncovers that their propensity to hedge is
15:568:40206:16:17:72:540:477:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:highly correlated with theirfinancing policies as well as their level of assets in place. In particular,
15:569:40310:17:16:72:539:460:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hefinds that the oil and gas producers in his sample that use more debtfinancing also hedge a
15:570:40403:16:16:72:540:444:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:greater fraction of their production, and he interprets this result as evidence that companies hedge
15:571:40503:16:17:72:282:428:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:to reduce the likelihood offinancial distress.
15:572:40549:17:16:88:540:411:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Given this theoretical and empirical motivation, we employ both balance-sheet and market-
15:573:40638:16:17:72:539:395:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:based measures of default risk as our empirical proxies for the cost of externalfinance. The balance-
15:574:40739:17:16:72:540:378:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:sheet based measure we employ is the Zmijewski (1984) score. This measure is positively related
15:575:40834:16:17:72:540:362:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:to default risk and is a variant of Altman’s (1968) Z-score, and the methodology employed to
15:576:40926:17:16:72:539:345:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:calculate the Zmijewski-score was developed by identifying thefirm-level balance-sheet variables
15:577:41022:16:16:72:540:329:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that help to “discriminate” whether afirm is likely to default or not. The market-based measures we
15:578:41121:16:17:72:539:313:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:employ arefirst (following Gilson (1989)), the rolling three-year average stock return of commodity
15:579:41220:17:16:72:540:296:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:producers, and second, the naive expected default frequency (or naive EDF) computed by Bharath
15:580:41314:16:17:72:175:280:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and Shumway (2008).
15:581:41333:17:29:88:301:263:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Eachfirm’s Zmijewski-score is calculated as:
15:582:41377:29:20:86:525:234:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f7:A:-=−43−45∗+57∗
15:583:41449:20:30:173:539:214:121:g_d0_f12:121:g_d0_f3:A:−0004∗(14)

15:585:41588:16:36:72:369:168:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:for afirmcalculated at the end of month,iscalculatedas:

16:592:41690:0:17:88:539:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, we obtain eachfirm’s naive EDF. The EDF from the KMV-Merton model is computed
16:593:41776:17:20:71:158:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:using the formula:
