16:602:41825:0:16:395:411:670:121:g_d0_f10:121:g_d0_f10:A:¶¶
16:603:41827:16:27:520:539:654:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:(16)
16:604:41831:27:16:72:539:627:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:whereis the total market value of thefirm,is the face value of thefirm’s debt,is the
16:605:41919:16:16:72:540:611:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:volatility of thefirm’s value,is an estimate of the expected annual return of thefirm’s assets,
16:606:42015:16:17:72:539:595:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:andis the time period (in this case, one year). Bharath and Shumway (2008) compute a ‘naive’
16:607:42108:17:16:72:540:578:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:estimate of the EDF, employing certain assumptions about the variable used as inputs into the
16:608:42201:16:17:72:540:562:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:formula above.  We use their estimates in our empirical analysis.12Of the set of 525firms, we
16:609:42294:17:16:72:263:545:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:have naive EDF estimates for 435firms.
16:610:42332:16:17:88:540:529:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:In the next section, wefirst confirm Haushalter’s (2000, 2001) results in our sample offirms —
16:611:42426:17:16:72:540:512:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:i.e., that our default risk measures are indeed related to individual producerfirms’ hedging activity.
16:612:42528:16:17:72:540:496:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:We then aggregate thesefirm-specific measures within each commodity sector to obtain aggregate
16:613:42622:17:16:72:539:479:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:measures of fundamental producer hedging demand,which are used to test the pricing implications
16:614:42717:16:16:72:540:463:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of the model. To arrive at these aggregate measures of producer’s hedging demand, we construct an
16:615:42814:16:17:72:540:447:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:equal-weighted Zmijewski-score, 3-year lagged stock returns, and Naive EDF from the producers
16:616:42907:17:16:72:539:430:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:in each commodity sector. While our sample offirms goes back until 1974, the number offirms in
16:617:43001:16:17:72:540:414:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:any given quarter varies with data availability at each point in time. There are, however, always
16:618:43098:17:16:72:540:397:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f7:B:more than 10firms underlying the aggregate hedging measure in any given quarter. Figures2
16:619:43188:16:17:72:539:381:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and2show the resulting time-series of aggregate Zmijewski-score, 3-year lagged return, and Naive
16:620:43285:17:16:72:540:364:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:EDF for the Crude Oil, Heating Oil, and Gasoline sectors, as well as for the Natural Gas sector.
16:621:43381:16:16:72:540:348:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:For ease of comparison, the series have been normalized to have zero mean and unit variance. All
16:622:43477:16:17:72:540:332:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the measures are persistent and stationary (the latter is confirmed in unreported unit root tests
16:623:43574:17:16:72:540:315:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:for all the measures). As expected, the aggregate Zmijewski-scores and Naive EDF’s are positively
16:624:43671:16:17:72:539:299:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:correlated, while the aggregate 3-year producer lagged stock return measure is negatively correlated
16:625:43771:17:16:72:539:282:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:with these measures. Table2reports the mean, standard deviation and quarterly autocorrelation of
16:626:43867:16:17:72:539:266:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the aggregate hedging measures. The reason that these summary statistics are different for Crude
16:627:43963:17:16:72:539:249:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Oil, Heating Oil, and Gasoline is that the futures returns data are of different sample sizes across
16:628:44063:16:38:72:154:233:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the commodities.
16:629:44079:38:27:72:304:195:209:g_d0_f2:209:g_d0_f2:C:4  Producers’ Hedging Behavior
16:630:44109:27:17:72:539:168:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:While the main tests in the paper concern the relationship between spot and futures commodity
16:631:44202:17:16:72:539:151:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:prices and the commodity sector’saggregatefundamental hedging demand, wefirst investigate the
16:632:44295:16:17:72:539:135:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:availablemicroevidence of producer hedging behavior. Haushalter (2000, 2001) provides useful
16:633:44387:17:16:72:539:118:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:evidence of the cross-sectional determinants of hedging behavior among oil and gasfirms, but his
16:634:44483:16:0:80:440:102:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:A:12We thank Sreedhar Bharath and Tyler Shumway for providing us with these estimates.
17:635:44569:0:17:72:540:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:evidence pertains to a smaller sample than ours, over the period from 1992 to 1994.13A natural
17:636:44663:17:16:71:540:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:question for our purposes is to what extent the oil and natural gas producingfirms in our sample
17:637:44759:16:17:71:539:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:actually do engage in hedging activity, and if so, in which derivative instruments and using what
17:638:44856:17:16:71:540:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:strategies. In this section, we use the publicly available data fromfirm accounting statements in the
17:639:44957:16:17:71:539:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:EDGAR database to ascertain the extent and nature of individual commodity producer hedging
17:640:45047:17:32:71:115:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:behavior.
17:641:45056:32:23:72:343:576:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:4.1  Summary of Producer Hedging Behavior
17:642:45097:23:17:72:540:553:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:The EDGAR database has available quarterly or annual statements for 231 of the 525firms in the
17:643:45191:17:16:72:540:536:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:sample. In part, the smaller EDGAR sample is due to the fact that derivative positions are only
17:644:45286:16:17:72:540:520:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:reported in accounting statements, in our sample, from 1998 onwards.14We determine whether
17:645:45376:17:16:71:540:503:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:or not eachfirm uses derivatives for hedging commodity price exposure by reading at least two
17:646:45469:16:16:71:539:487:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:quarterly or annual reports perfirm. Panel A in Table1shows that out of the 231firms, there are
17:647:45564:16:17:71:539:471:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:172 that explicitly state that they use commodity derivatives, 20 that explicitly state that they do
17:648:45664:17:16:71:540:454:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f3:B:notuse commodity derivatives, and 39 that don’t mention any use of derivatives. Of the 172firms
17:649:45759:16:17:71:539:438:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that use commodity derivatives, Panel B shows that 146 explicitly state that they use derivatives
17:650:45856:17:16:71:540:421:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f3:B:onlyfor hedging purposes, while 16firms say they both hedge and speculate. For the remaining
17:651:45948:16:17:71:539:405:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:10firms, we cannot tell. In sum, 74% of the producers in the EDGAR sample state that they use
17:652:46041:17:16:71:540:388:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:commodity derivatives, while a maximum of 26% of thefirms do not use commodity derivatives.
17:653:46132:16:16:71:459:372:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Of thefirms that use derivatives, 85% are, by their own admission, pure hedgers.
17:654:46212:16:17:88:539:356:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Panel C of Table1shows the instruments thefirms use and their relative proportions. Forwards
17:655:46304:17:16:71:539:339:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and futures are used in 29% of thefirms, while swaps are used by 52% of thefirms.  Options
17:656:46394:16:17:71:540:323:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and strategies, such as put and call spreads and collars, are used by 20% and 33% of thefirms,
17:657:46488:17:16:71:539:306:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:respectively. Most options positions are not strong volatility bets. In particular, low-cost collars
17:658:46588:16:17:71:539:290:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that are long out-of-the-money put and short out-of-the-money calls are the most common option
17:659:46682:17:16:71:539:273:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:strategy for producers — a position that is very similar to a short futures position. Thus, derivative
17:660:46784:16:17:71:540:257:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hedging strategies that are linear, or close to linear, in the underlying are by far the most common.
17:661:46885:17:16:88:539:240:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:We focus on short-term commodity futures - the most liquid derivative instruments in the
17:662:46973:16:16:71:539:224:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:commodity markets - in our empirical analysis. However, a considerable fraction of the hedging
17:663:47067:16:15:80:539:208:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:13Another notable study offirm-level hedging behavior in commodities is Tufano (1996), who relies on proprietary
17:664:47179:15:7:71:187:193:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:data from gold miningfirms.
17:665:47206:7:15:80:539:186:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:14Since the introduction of Financial Accounting Standards Board’s 133 regulation (Accounting for Derivative
17:666:47314:15:11:71:539:171:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:Instruments and Hedging Activities), effective forfiscal years beginning after June 15, 2000,firms are required
17:667:47425:11:11:71:540:160:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:to measure allfinancial assets and liabilities on company balance sheets at fair value. In particular, hedging and
17:668:47539:11:10:71:539:149:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:derivative activities are usually disclosed in two places. Risk exposures and the accounting policy relating to the use of
17:669:47661:10:11:71:539:139:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:derivatives are included in “Market Risk Information.” Any unusual impact on earnings resulting from accounting for
17:670:47776:11:11:71:539:128:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:derivatives should be explained in the “Results of Operations.” Additionally, a further discussion of risk management
17:671:47893:11:11:71:539:117:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:activity is provided in a footnote disclosure titled “Risk Management Activities & Derivative Financial Instruments.”
17:672:48010:11:0:71:448:106:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:Somefirms, however, provided some information on derivative positions also before this date.
18:673:48104:0:17:72:540:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:is done with swaps, which are provided by banks over-the-counter, and often are longer term. On
18:674:48199:17:16:72:539:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the one hand, this indicates that a significant proportion of producer’s hedging is done outside
18:675:48295:16:17:72:540:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the futures markets that we consider. On the other hand, banks in turn hedge their aggregate
18:676:48387:17:16:72:540:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:net exposure in the underlying futures market and in the most liquid contracts. For instance, it is
18:677:48486:16:17:72:540:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:common to hedge long-term exposure by rolling over short-term contracts (e.g., Metallgesellschaft).
18:678:48585:17:16:72:540:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:A similar argument can be made for the net commodity option imbalance held by banks in the
18:679:48675:16:16:72:540:592:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:aggregate. Therefore, producers’ aggregate net hedging pressure is likely to be reflected in trades
18:680:48774:16:32:72:285:576:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:in the underlying short-term futures market.
18:681:48818:32:24:72:383:544:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:4.2  The Time-Series Behavior of Producer Hedging
18:682:48867:24:16:72:540:520:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Information about hedging positions from accounting statements could potentially be used directly
18:683:48964:16:16:72:540:504:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:to assess the impact of time-varying producer hedging demand on commodity returns. However,
18:684:49055:16:17:72:539:488:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:there are significant data limitations for such use. First, FAS 133 requires thefirms to report mark-
18:685:49156:17:16:72:539:471:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:to-market values of derivative positions, which are not directly informative about underlying price
18:686:49255:16:17:72:539:455:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:exposure. There is no agreed upon reporting standard or requirement for providing information
18:687:49348:17:16:72:540:438:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:on effective price exposure for eachfirm’s derivative positions, which leads to either non-reporting,
18:688:49449:16:17:72:540:422:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:or very different reporting of such information.  For instance,firms sometimes report notional
18:689:49543:17:16:72:540:405:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:outstanding or number of barrels underlying a contract, but not the direction of the position or the
18:690:49643:16:16:72:540:389:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:actual derivative instruments and contracts used, the 5%-, 10%-, or 20%-delta with respect to the
18:691:49740:16:17:72:539:373:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:underlying, or Value-at-Risk measures (again sometimes without mention of direction of hedge).
18:692:49834:17:16:72:540:356:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:We went throughallthe quarterly and annual reports available for thefirms with SIC codes 2910
18:693:49927:16:17:72:540:340:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and 2911 (50firms) in the EDGAR database to attempt to extract (a) whether thefirms were long
18:694:50020:17:16:72:540:323:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:or short the underlying, and (b) the extent of exposure in each quarter or year as measured by
18:695:50114:16:17:72:532:307:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:sensitivity to price changes in the underlying commodity futures price (i.e., a measure of Delta).
18:696:50212:17:16:88:540:290:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:PanelDinTable1reports that of the 34firms with these SIC codes that we couldfind in
18:697:50295:16:17:71:539:274:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:EDGAR, only 19 (56%) gave information about the direction of the hedge (long or short the
18:698:50384:17:16:71:540:257:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:underlying). Of these, 80%, on average, of thefirm-date observations were short the underlying
18:699:50478:16:16:71:539:241:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:commodity. Since commodity producers are naturally long the commodity, one would expect that
18:700:50570:16:17:71:540:225:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the producers’ derivative hedge positions are always short the underlying.  However, there are
18:701:50664:17:16:71:540:208:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:complicating factors. First, somefirms do take speculative positions. Second, there are cases where
18:702:50763:16:17:71:539:192:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hedging demand could manifest itself in long positions in the futures market. For instance, a pure
18:703:50861:17:16:71:540:175:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:refiner may have an incentive to go long crude oil futures to hedge its input costs, but short,
18:704:50956:16:17:71:539:159:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:say gasoline futures to hedge its production. This suggests that it might be fruitful to separate
18:705:51053:17:16:71:539:142:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:producers and producer refiners (such as Marathon Oil) from pure refiners (such as Frontier Oil)
18:706:51149:16:16:72:318:126:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:in the analysis, and we do so as a robustness check.
18:707:51201:16:17:88:540:110:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Of the 19firms that reported whether they were long or short in the futures markets, we could
18:708:51294:17:0:72:540:93:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:only extract a reliable, and relatively long, time-series of derivative position exposure to the under-
19:709:51399:0:17:72:540:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:lying commodity price for 4firms: Marathon Oil, Hess Corporation, Valero Energy Corporation,
19:710:51491:17:16:71:539:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and Frontier Oil Corporation. Consequently, the data is not rich enough to provide a measure
19:711:51583:16:17:71:539:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:ofaggregateproducer hedging positions based on direct (self-reported) observations of producers’
19:712:51679:17:16:72:540:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:futures hedging demand, even for the relatively short period for which EDGAR data is available.
19:713:51774:16:17:72:540:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Nevertheless, we show the relationship between the time series of hedging behavior and default
19:714:51868:17:16:72:539:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:risk for the 4firms for which we were able to extract this information. This represents an interest-
19:715:51968:16:16:72:540:592:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:ing insight into the time-series variation in hedging, which complements existing analyses (such as
19:716:52067:16:17:72:540:576:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Haushalter (2000, 2001)) of the cross-sectional relation between hedging behavior and default risk
19:717:52165:17:32:72:118:559:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:measures.
19:718:52174:32:23:72:369:527:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:4.3  Observed Hedging Demand and Default Risk
19:719:52219:23:16:72:540:504:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:From the quarterly and annual reports of these fourfirms, we extract a measure of eachfirm’s
19:720:52311:16:17:72:540:488:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:$1 delta exposure to the price of crude oil (i.e., how does the value of the company’s derivative
19:721:52408:17:16:72:540:471:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:position change if the price of the underlying increases by $1). This measure of eachfirm’s hedging
19:722:52507:16:17:71:540:455:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:position is constructed from, for instance, value-at-risk numbers that are provided in the reports
19:723:52605:17:16:71:539:438:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:by assuming log-normal price movements and using the historical mean and volatility from the
19:724:52697:16:17:71:540:422:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:respective commodity futures returns. In other cases,firms report delta’s based on 5%, 10% and
19:725:52791:17:16:71:539:405:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:20% moves in the underlying price, which are then used to construct the $1 delta number as a
19:726:52883:16:16:71:207:389:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:measure of hedging demand.
19:727:52909:16:17:88:540:373:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:We next compare the time-series of each of thefirms’ commodity derivatives hedging demand
19:728:52998:17:16:71:539:356:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:to eachfirm’s Zmijewski-score and 3-year lagged stock return throughout the EDGAR sample.
19:729:53087:16:17:71:539:340:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:There are too few observations perfirm to compare with the naive-EDF scores, which is only
19:730:53177:17:16:71:539:323:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:provided to us until the end of 2003. Figure3shows the negative of the imputed delta and the
19:731:53270:16:17:71:539:307:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Zmijewski-score for each of the four companies. Both variables are normalized to have mean zero
19:732:53365:17:16:71:540:290:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and unit variance. Thefigure shows that there is a strong, positive correlation between the level
19:733:53462:16:17:71:540:274:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of default risk, as measured by the Zmijewski-score and the amount of short exposure to crude oil
19:734:53559:17:16:71:539:257:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:using derivative positions for Marathon Oil, Hess Corp., and Valero Energy Corp. For Frontier Oil
19:735:53656:16:16:71:539:241:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Corp., the hedging activity is strongly negatively correlated with the Zmijewski-score. The same
19:736:53752:16:17:71:539:225:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:pattern can be seen in Figure3,whereeachfirm’s hedging activity is plotted against the negative
19:737:53848:17:16:71:540:208:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of its 3-year average stock returns. Marathon Oil and Hess both extract and refine oil and so it is
19:738:53947:16:17:71:540:192:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:natural that as default risk and hedging demand increases, thesefirms increase their short crude
19:739:54043:17:16:72:540:175:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:oil positions. Valero, however, is a pure refining company that one might argue should go more
19:740:54137:16:17:72:540:159:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f3:B:longcrude oil as default risk increases. This does not happen, however, because Valero in fact
19:741:54231:17:16:72:539:142:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:holds inventory of its input, crude oil, as well as for refined products. This was inferred by reading
19:742:54333:16:16:72:539:126:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Valero’s quarterly reports, and is anecdotally quite a common happenstance for refiners. Thus, an
19:743:54430:16:17:72:540:110:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:increase in the demand for hedging leads to increasing hedge of both the input and output good
19:744:54524:17:0:72:540:93:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:inventories. Frontier Oil, however, behaves more as one might naively expect of a refiner, as the
20:745:54623:0:17:72:539:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:company does not hold significant crude inventory in this sample, and decreases its short crude
20:746:54718:17:16:72:540:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:positions as default risk increases. Finally, as a check that the proxies used capture default risk in
20:747:54820:16:17:72:540:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:our sample, Figure3shows the time-series relation between Valero’s 5-year CDS spread (obtained
20:748:54915:17:16:71:539:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:from Markit) and its short crude oil hedging. Valero is the only of thesefirms where CDS data was
20:749:55012:16:17:72:460:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:available to us. Again, we see a strong relation between hedging and default risk.
20:750:55094:17:16:88:540:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:In sum, in these fourfirms, which constituted the best sample available in EDGAR of the
20:751:55181:16:16:72:540:592:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:producerfirms, it is clear that hedging activity is time-varying, and related to the proposed proxies
20:752:55282:16:17:72:540:576:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:for fundamental hedging demand. However, the graphs highlight that one must take care when
20:753:55372:17:16:72:539:559:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:inferring expected hedging activity from whether afirm is involved only with extraction, extraction
20:754:55471:16:17:72:540:543:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and refining, or purely refining. Essentially, allfirms are to some extent naturally long crude oil,
20:755:55571:17:16:72:543:526:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:but for pure refiners,thisislikelylesstruethanforcompaniesthatengageinbothextractionas
20:756:55657:16:17:72:396:510:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:well as refining - echoing the analysis in Ederington and Lee (2002).
20:757:55726:17:16:88:539:493:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:We now turn to our analysis of theaggregaterelationships between our proxies for fundamental
20:758:55818:16:17:72:540:477:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hedging demand, spot returns and futures risk premia in the oil and gas markets. We will, however,
20:759:55916:17:16:72:539:460:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:use the non-hedgingfirms identified in the micro-analysis in this section and the separation between
20:760:56016:16:38:72:483:444:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:producers and refiners to perform robustness checks for our aggregate results to come.
20:761:56102:38:27:72:306:406:209:g_d0_f2:209:g_d0_f2:C:5  Aggregate Empirical Analysis
20:762:56133:27:17:72:539:379:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:In this section, we employ the aggregate measures of producer hedging demand, for which we
20:763:56223:17:16:72:540:362:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:reported summary statistics in the Data section, to test the empirical predictions of the model
20:764:56318:16:32:72:192:346:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:documented in Section2.
20:765:56341:32:24:72:319:314:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:5.1  Commodity Futures and Spot Prices
20:766:56379:24:16:72:540:290:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Our commodity futures price data is for NYMEX contracts and is obtained from Datastream. The
20:767:56471:16:17:72:539:274:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:longest futures return sample period available in Datastream goes from thefirst quarter of 1980
20:768:56566:17:16:72:345:257:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:until the fourth quarter of 2006 (108 quarters; crude oil).
20:769:56625:16:17:88:539:241:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:To create the basis and returns measures, we follow the methodology of Gorton, Hayashi and
20:770:56715:17:16:72:540:224:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Rouwenhorst (2007). We construct rolling commodity futures excess returns at the end of each
20:771:56807:16:17:72:539:208:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:month as the one-period price difference in the nearest to maturity contract that would not expire
20:772:56905:17:16:72:539:191:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:during the next month. That is, the excess return from the end of monthto the next is calculated
20:773:57002:16:9:72:85:175:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:as:
20:774:57005:9:15:273:333:166:121:g_d0_f7:65:g_d0_f8:?:+1−
20:775:57016:15:0:294:311:151:121:g_d0_f7:65:g_d0_f8:?:
20:776:57020:0:28:336:539:159:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f3:A:(17)
20:777:57025:28:16:71:539:131:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:whereis the futures price at the end of monthon the nearest contract whose expiration date
20:778:57120:16:16:72:540:115:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f3:B:is after the end of month+1,and+1is the price of the same contract at the end of month
20:779:57212:16:0:71:539:99:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f3:B:+1. The quarterly return is constructed as the product of the three monthly gross returns in the
21:780:57311:0:17:72:110:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:quarter.
21:781:57319:17:16:88:539:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The futures basis is calculated for each commodity as(12−1),where1is the nearest
21:782:57403:16:17:72:539:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:futures contract and2is the next nearest futures contract.  Summary statistics about these
21:783:57494:17:16:72:540:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:quarterly measures are presented in Table2. Note that the means and medians of the basis in the
21:784:57589:16:17:72:540:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:table are computed using the raw data, while the standard deviation andfirst-order autocorrelation
21:785:57687:17:16:72:540:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:coefficient are computed using the deseasonalized basis, where the deseasonalized basis is simply
21:786:57784:16:16:72:539:592:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the residual from a regression of the actual basis onfour quarterly dummies. The basis is persistent
21:787:57884:16:17:72:375:576:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:across all commodities once seasonality has been accounted for.
21:788:57947:17:16:88:540:559:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Table2further shows that the excess returns are on average positive for all three commodities,
21:789:58041:16:17:71:539:543:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:ranging from25%to67%, with relatively large standard deviations (overall in excess of20%). As
21:790:58136:17:16:72:540:526:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:expected, the sample autocorrelations of excess returns on the futures are close to zero. The spot
21:791:58234:16:17:72:540:510:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:returns are defined using the nearest-to-expiration futures contract, again consistent with Gorton,
21:792:58333:17:11:72:233:493:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Hayashi and Rouwenhorst (2007):
21:793:58364:11:15:265:343:482:121:g_d0_f7:65:g_d0_f11:?:+1+2−+1
21:794:58379:15:0:291:317:467:121:g_d0_f7:65:g_d0_f11:?:+1
21:795:58385:0:27:344:539:475:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f3:A:(18)
21:796:58390:27:17:72:540:448:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Again, the quarterly return is constructed by aggregating monthly returns as defined above. Note
21:797:58486:17:16:72:540:431:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that the spot returns display negative autocorrelation, consistent with mean-reversion in the level
21:798:58585:16:32:72:153:415:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of the spot price.
21:799:58603:32:24:72:159:383:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:5.2  Inventory
21:800:58617:24:16:72:540:359:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:For all four energy commodities, aggregate U.S. inventories are obtained from the Department
21:801:58709:16:17:72:540:343:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of Energy’s Monthly Energy Review.  For Crude Oil, we use the item: “U.S. crude oil ending
21:802:58799:17:16:72:540:326:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:stocks non-SPR, thousands of barrels.” For Heating Oil, we use the item: “U.S. total distillate
21:803:58894:16:17:72:540:310:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:stocks”. For Gasoline, we use: “U.S. total motorgasoline ending stocks, thousands of barrels.”
21:804:58988:17:16:72:540:293:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Finally, for Natural Gas, we use: “U.S. totalnatural gas in underground storage (working gas),
21:805:59082:16:17:72:540:277:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:millions of cubic feet.” Following Gorton, Hayashi and Rouwenhorst (2007), we compute a measure
21:806:59177:17:16:72:540:260:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of the discretionary level of aggregate inventory by subtracting a moving trend of inventory from
21:807:59274:16:16:72:540:244:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the quarterly realized inventory (so as to avoid look-ahead bias).  Quarterly trend inventory is
21:808:59370:16:17:72:540:228:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:created using a Hodrick-Prescottfilter with the recommended smoothing parameter (1600). In all
21:809:59464:17:16:71:540:211:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:specifications that employ inventories, we also include quarterly dummy variables, to control for
21:810:59561:16:17:71:539:195:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the strong seasonality present in inventories. Table2shows summary statistics of the resulting
21:811:59655:17:16:71:539:178:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:aggregate inventory measure, i.e., the cyclical component of inventory stocks, for the commodities.
21:812:59754:16:0:71:539:162:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Once the seasonality in inventories is accounted for, the trend deviations in inventory are persistent.
22:813:59859:0:24:72:239:691:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:5.3  Hedger Positions Data.
22:814:59886:24:16:72:540:667:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:The Commodity Futures Trading Commission (CFTC) reports aggregate data on net “hedger”
22:815:59972:16:17:72:540:651:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:positions in a variety of commodity futures contracts. These data have been used in several papers
22:816:60070:17:16:72:539:634:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that arrive at differing conclusions about their usefulness.  For example, Gorton, Hayashi and
22:817:60164:16:17:71:540:618:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Rouwenhorst (2007)find that this measure of hedger demand does not significantly forecast forward
22:818:60261:17:16:71:540:601:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:risk premiums, while De Roon, Nijman and Veld (2000)find that they hold some forecasting power
22:819:60355:16:17:71:540:585:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:for futures risk premia. The CFTC hedging classification has significant shortcomings; in particular,
22:820:60456:17:16:72:540:568:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:anyone that can reasonably argue that they have a cash position in the underlying can obtain a
22:821:60550:16:16:72:540:552:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hedger classification.  This includes consumers of the commodity, and more prominently, banks
22:822:60643:16:17:72:539:536:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that have offsetting positions in the commodity (perhaps on account of holding a position in the
22:823:60739:17:16:71:543:519:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:swap market). The line between a hedge trade and a speculative trade, as definedbythismeasure,
22:824:60833:16:17:71:539:503:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:is therefore blurred. We note these issues with the measure as they may help explain why the
22:825:60925:17:16:71:540:486:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:forecasting power of hedging pressure for futures risk premia is debatable, while our measures of
22:826:61022:16:17:71:539:470:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:default risk do seem to explain futures risk premia. Nevertheless, we use the CFTC data as a check
22:827:61120:17:16:71:539:453:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that our measures of producers’ hedging demand is in fact reflected in futures positions as noted
22:828:61217:16:16:71:138:437:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:by the CFTC.
22:829:61229:16:17:88:539:421:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The Hedger Net Positions data are obtained from Pinnacle Inc., which sources data directly from
22:830:61324:17:16:71:540:404:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the Commodity Futures Trading Commission (CFTC). Classification into Hedgers, Speculators and
22:831:61417:16:17:71:539:388:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Small traders is done by the CFTC, and the reported data are the total open positions, both short
22:832:61514:17:16:71:539:371:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and long, of each of these trader types across all maturities of futures contracts. We measure the
22:833:61612:16:32:71:282:355:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:net position of all hedgers in each period as:
22:834:61658:32:0:97:215:323:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f9:?:=
22:835:61678:0:15:230:479:330:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f9:?:(−)
22:836:61722:15:0:219:490:315:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f9:?:(−1+−1)
22:837:61770:0:32:492:539:323:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f3:A:(19)
22:838:61775:32:17:71:539:291:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:This normalization means that the net positions are measured relative to the aggregate open interest
22:839:61875:17:16:71:544:274:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of hedgers in the previous quarter. Summary statistics on these data are shown in Table2.First,
22:840:61970:16:17:71:539:258:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the hedger positions are on average positive, which means investors classified as “hedgers” are
22:841:62065:17:16:72:540:241:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:on average short the commodity forwards. However, the standard deviations are relatively large,
22:842:62160:16:16:72:540:225:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:indicating that there are times when the CFTC classified “hedgers” are actually net long commodity
22:843:62258:16:33:72:155:209:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:futures contracts.
22:844:62276:33:23:72:217:176:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:5.4  Aggregate Controls
22:845:62299:23:17:72:540:153:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:In our empirical tests, we use controls to account for sources of risk premia that are not due to
22:846:62396:17:16:72:540:136:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hedging pressure. In a standard asset pricing setting, time-varying aggregate risk aversion and/or
22:847:62494:16:16:72:539:120:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:aggregate risk can give rise to time-variation in excess returns.  This is reflected in the pricing
22:848:62593:16:0:72:539:104:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:kernel,Λ, of equity-holders in the model. To capture this source of variation, therefore, we include
23:849:62695:0:17:72:540:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:business cycle variables that have been shown to forecast excess asset returns in previous research.
23:850:62795:17:16:88:540:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:We include the Default Spread: the difference between the Baa and Aaa rated corporate bond
23:851:62885:16:17:71:539:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:yields, which proxies for aggregate default risk in the economy and has been shown to forecast
23:852:62979:17:16:71:539:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:excess returns on stocks and bonds (see, e.g., Fama and French (1989), and Jagannathan and Wang
23:853:63074:16:17:71:540:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:(1996)). Following Harrison and Yogo (2009), we also include the Term Spread, constructed as the
23:854:63170:17:16:71:539:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:difference between the yield on a 5-year zero-coupon T-bond and the yield on the 3-month T-bill. We
23:855:63269:16:16:71:539:592:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:do not include the aggregate dividend yield, as this variable has no forecasting power for commodity
23:856:63369:16:17:71:539:576:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:returns (results available on request). Finally, to account for time-varying expected commodity spot
23:857:63469:17:16:71:539:559:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:demand, we use a forecast of quarterly GDP growth, obtained from the Philadelphia Fed’s survey
23:858:63563:16:33:71:196:543:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of professional forecasters.
23:859:63591:33:23:72:274:510:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:5.5  Commodity Specific Controls
23:860:63623:23:16:72:540:487:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:We also include controls that are specific to each commodity. As emphasized in Gorton, Hayashi,
23:861:63718:16:17:71:539:471:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and Rouwenhorst (2008), the cyclical level of inventory is related to the conditional volatility of the
23:862:63821:17:16:71:539:454:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:commodity price, and as such, the volatility of spot and futures returns. The basis is related to (the
23:863:63923:16:17:71:539:438:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:probability) of an inventory stock-out, and so is expected to have predictive power mainly for the
23:864:64021:17:16:71:539:421:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:spot return. When there is ample inventory, however, the basis is not expected to be informative
23:865:64117:16:17:71:539:405:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:about spot or futures returns, and so it should not drive out predictability that arises from producer
23:866:64219:17:16:72:540:388:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hedging demand. The lagged futures return is included to capture autocorrelation in excess futures
23:867:64317:16:17:72:540:372:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:returns not captured by the other controls. A component of the measures of producer default risk
23:868:64413:17:16:72:539:355:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:will be related to lagged commodity returns (asfirm performance is related to commodity returns),
23:869:64510:16:16:72:540:339:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and we want to ensure that the proxies for producer hedging demand are not simply capturing this
23:870:64606:16:17:72:540:323:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:autocorrelation in commodity returns. Finally, we include quarterly dummy variables in all the
23:871:64700:17:16:72:540:306:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:regressions as both the independent and many of the dependent variables in the regressions exhibit
23:872:64798:16:32:72:133:290:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:seasonalities.
23:873:64812:32:24:72:207:258:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:5.6  Empirical Results
23:874:64834:24:16:72:540:234:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Before we test the predictions of the model with respect to the expected commodity futures and spot
23:875:64933:16:17:72:539:218:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:return, wefirst perform an additional check of the validity of theaggregatemeasures of producers’
23:876:65030:17:16:71:539:201:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:fundamental hedging demand by relating them to the CFTC measures of aggregate net hedging
23:877:65119:16:17:71:539:185:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:demand. As previously explained, the aggregate CFTC data on hedger positions is noisy. However,
23:878:65214:17:16:71:539:168:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:a noisy measure of hedger positions should still contain information about the underlying true
23:879:65308:16:0:71:198:152:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:producer hedging demand.
24:880:65334:0:24:72:427:691:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:C:5.6.1  CFTC Hedging Positions and Producer Hedging Demand
24:881:65391:24:16:72:540:667:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:We construct the hedger net position variables from the CFTC data as the netshortposition, so
24:882:65484:16:17:71:539:651:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f9:B:we should expect a positive relation between the default risk and CFTC hedger positions. Table3
24:883:65579:17:30:71:243:634:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:reports the results of the regression:
24:884:65617:30:29:158:539:604:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f3:A:=+ +(20)
24:885:65674:29:17:72:539:575:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:wheredenotes the relevant commodity (crude oil, heating oil, gasoline, or natural gas).  The
24:886:65767:17:16:72:539:558:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:term "ControlVariables" is a catch-all term for the inclusion of the control variables described
24:887:65863:16:17:72:539:542:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:earlier, and “” denotes the average producer Zmijewski-score, the average producer Naive
24:888:65958:17:16:72:540:525:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:EDF, or thenegativeof the 3-year average producer stock returns (so as to make the expected
24:889:66049:16:16:72:539:509:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:regression coefficient,, positive in all specifications).  In these regressions, both the left- and
24:890:66150:16:17:72:539:493:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:right-hand side variables are normalized to have unit variance, so the regression coefficients can be
24:891:66251:17:16:72:539:476:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:easily interpreted. Table3shows that10out of12of the regression coefficients(0)are positive
24:892:66344:16:17:72:540:460:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and that half are positive and significant at the10%level or greater at the individual commodity
24:893:66440:17:16:71:539:443:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:level. The significance level is overall increasing in the number of observations available (Natural
24:894:66540:16:17:71:539:427:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Gas and Gasoline have the fewest observations and largely insignificant coefficients). To alleviate
24:895:66639:17:16:72:539:410:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:issues regarding power, we present in the right-most column of Table3the-coefficients from
24:896:66730:16:16:72:539:394:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f3:B:pooledregressions across all commodities for all the default risk measures. In all three cases, the
24:897:66829:16:17:72:539:378:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:regression coefficient is positive and significant at the5%level.15Thus, the aggregate measures
24:898:66924:17:16:71:540:361:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of producer hedging demand are indeed significantly and positively related to the CFTC recorded
24:899:67019:16:32:71:211:345:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:aggregate "hedger" positions.
24:900:67048:32:24:71:268:313:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:C:5.6.2  Commodity Futures Returns
24:901:67080:24:16:71:539:289:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Next,weevaluatethefirst part of Proposition1, namely that increases in fundamental hedging
24:902:67170:16:16:71:539:273:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:demand are associated with higher futures risk premia. To do so, we run a standard forecasting
24:903:67264:16:17:71:540:257:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:regression for excess commodity futures return, using our default risk proxy for fundamental hedging
24:904:67364:17:16:71:539:240:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:demand. In particular, we regress quarterly (excess) futures returns on one quarter lagged measures
24:905:67463:16:30:71:244:224:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of default risk and control variables:
24:906:67501:30:30:147:539:194:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f3:A:+1=+ ++1(21)
24:907:67563:30:16:71:422:164:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:wheredenotes the commodity anddenotes time measured in quarters.
24:908:67629:16:16:88:539:148:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Table4shows the results of the above regression across the four commodities considered, as
24:909:67719:16:15:80:539:132:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:15Note that in all individual-commodity regressions in this paper, standard errors are constructed using the Newey-
24:910:67834:15:11:71:539:117:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:West (1987) method, which is robust to heteroskedasticity and autocorrelation of the error terms, and in all pooled
24:911:67949:11:11:71:539:106:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:regressions, we employ Rogers (1983, 1993) errors that are robust to heteroskedasticity, own and cross-autocorrelation
24:912:68067:11:0:71:365:95:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:and contemporaneous correlation across all commodities in each quarter.
25:913:68140:0:17:72:540:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:well as a pooled regression across all commodities. First, we note that in all cases, the regression
25:914:68240:17:16:72:539:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:coefficients have the predicted sign: an increase in default risk forecasts higher futures returns over
25:915:68343:16:17:72:540:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the next quarter. For ease of interpretation, the default risk measures are in all cases normalized
25:916:68442:17:16:72:539:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:to have unit variance, and thus the regression coefficients give the expected futures return response
25:917:68543:16:17:72:540:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:to a one standard deviation change in the aggregate default risk measure. The average expected
25:918:68637:17:16:72:540:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:return response is highly economically significant at4%per quarter across the commodities. The
25:919:68731:16:16:72:540:592:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f9:B:standard deviation of quarterly futures returns of Crude Oil, Heating Oil, and Gasoline is20%
25:920:68824:16:17:72:540:576:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:per quarter, and so the implied quarterly2from the effect of the producer fundamental hedging
25:921:68918:17:16:71:540:559:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:demand alone is4%for these commodities.  This is high for a quarterly forecasting regression,
25:922:69011:16:17:71:419:543:121:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:B:considering the high persistence of thepredictive default risk variables.16
25:923:69086:17:16:88:539:526:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f9:A:The pooled regressions show that the effect of producer hedging demand is significant at the5%
25:924:69180:16:17:71:539:510:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:level or greater for all the default measures. In the individual regressions, the evidence is strongest
25:925:69283:17:16:71:539:493:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:for Crude Oil, Heating Oil and Gasoline, and somewhat weaker for Natural Gas. However, the the
25:926:69377:16:17:71:540:477:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:latter has the shortest time-series (49and63quarters when using the naive EDF or the two other
25:927:69471:17:16:71:539:460:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:default risk measures, respectively), which potentially explains the lower significance. Furthermore,
25:928:69572:16:16:71:539:444:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Haushalter (2000, 2001) points out that hedging for Natural Gas producers in particular is less
25:929:69667:16:17:71:539:428:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:prevalent and more risky since there is substantial basis risk depending on the location of the
25:930:69762:17:16:71:540:411:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:producer relative to the location at which the benchmark price is set.17This may also be responsible
25:931:69862:16:17:72:463:395:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:for the somewhat weaker results we see for this commodity throughout the paper.
25:932:69941:17:16:88:540:378:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:In sum, we conclude that there is strong evidence that commodity producers’ fundamental
25:933:70028:16:17:72:540:362:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hedging demand is positively related to the expected return of commodity futures, consistent with
25:934:70125:17:31:72:447:345:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the model in Section2. Next, we report three robustness checks of our results.
25:935:70203:31:17:88:539:314:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f3:A:Volatility Interaction.From the expression for the futures risk premium in Equation (11),
25:936:70292:17:16:72:540:297:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the model implies an interaction between fundamental hedging demand () and the commodity
25:937:70382:16:17:71:540:281:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:futures return volatility. In particular, a changein fundamental hedging demand has a larger impact
25:938:70481:17:29:71:530:264:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:on the futures risk premium if volatility is high. We test this relation by running the regression:
25:939:70580:29:17:71:543:235:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f7:F:+1=1+2+3×+ ++1
25:940:70671:17:16:520:539:218:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:(22)
25:941:70675:16:17:72:540:202:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:wheredenotes the commodity,denotes time measured in quarters, andis a measure of the
25:942:70766:17:16:71:539:185:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:conditional variance at timeof futures returns from timeto+1for commodity(the realized
25:943:70856:16:17:71:539:169:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:variance). The model predicts a positive coefficient on the interaction term(3). Since volatility
25:944:70956:17:15:80:539:152:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:16The default risk measures are also significant predictors of futures returns in simple univariate regressions (not
25:945:71072:15:7:72:112:137:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:reported).
25:946:71082:7:15:80:540:130:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:17He mentions, for example, that in 1993 the correlation between the prices of natural gas sold at Wheeling Ridge
25:947:71195:15:11:71:539:115:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:HubinCaliforniaandgassoldatHenryHubinLouisiana (the benchmark for prices on NYMEX contracts) was
25:948:71291:11:0:71:159:104:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:slightly less than 30%
26:949:71315:0:17:72:540:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:also appears in the covariance term in Equation (11), it is important to include its direct effect.
26:950:71414:17:16:71:539:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Further, the conditional volatility of futures returns is an indirect control for supply uncertainty
26:951:71514:16:17:71:540:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:(probability of inventory stock-out or other production shocks) that may be correlated with default
26:952:71613:17:16:71:539:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:risk. The estimate of the conditional variance we use is the realized average squared daily futures
26:953:71712:16:17:71:539:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:returns from timeto+1. The use of the realized variance as the volatility measure is convenient
26:954:71809:17:16:71:540:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:as there are both seasonalities and trends in volatility over the sample. Table5shows the results
26:955:71906:16:16:71:539:592:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of the above regression, where all the independent variables are normalized to have zero mean
26:956:71999:16:17:71:539:576:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and unit variance. Focusing on the pooled regression results in the rightmost column, we see that
26:957:72096:17:16:71:540:559:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:including the volatility interaction term increases the average response (2) from its level in Table
26:958:72197:16:17:72:539:543:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f3:B:4,from4%to about6%.Theeffect is significant for all the default risk measures and the signs are
26:959:72292:17:31:71:198:526:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:as predicted by the model.
26:960:72318:31:17:88:539:495:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f3:A:Producersversusrefiners.Next, we consider the forecasting power of the default risk
26:961:72401:17:16:71:539:478:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:measures based on allfirms in our sample, as before, versus the subset offirms that state they are
26:962:72499:16:17:71:540:462:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:solely refiners. To separate these two groups, we peruse the accounting statements from EDGAR
26:963:72592:17:16:71:540:445:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:tofindfirms that are solely refiners. As discussed in Section3, pure play refiners may hedge short
26:964:72690:16:17:71:539:429:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:crude oil if they store crude, but if they do not they have an incentive to hedge by going long as
26:965:72788:17:16:71:539:412:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:they use crude oil as an input good. Thus, aggregate default risk measures based only on pure play
26:966:72886:16:17:71:539:396:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:refiners’ data should forecast futures returns with a negative sign (per the results for Frontier Oil
26:967:72987:17:16:71:540:379:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:discussed in Section3), when combined with the default risk measures that we have been using
26:968:73079:16:30:71:463:363:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that are derived from allfirms in the sample. In particular, we run the regression:
26:969:73162:30:29:77:539:333:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f3:A:+1=1_+2_+ ++1(23)
26:970:73240:29:17:71:540:304:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f7:B:where_are the aggregate default risk measures used before, and_
26:971:73328:17:16:71:540:287:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:are the default risk measures constructed using onlyfirms that are identified as pure play refin-
26:972:73425:16:17:72:540:271:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:ers. The independent variable () is the one-period-ahead return on crude oil futures.
26:973:73521:17:16:72:539:254:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Table6shows that all the default risk measures based on pure play refiners come in negative, as
26:974:73616:16:17:72:539:238:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:conjectured, and significant for the Zmijewski-score and lagged negative 3-year stock returns. The
26:975:73714:17:16:72:540:221:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Table also shows the corresponding forecasting regression for changes in the spot price, which yield
26:976:73814:16:32:72:142:205:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:similar results.
26:977:73830:32:16:88:540:173:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f3:A:Hedgers versus Non-Hedgers.Next, we consider the forecasting power of default risk mea-
26:978:73917:16:17:72:540:157:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:sures based on producers that state they are hedgers, and contrast these measures with measures
26:979:74012:17:16:72:540:140:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:derived from producers that are stated non-hedgers. First, we use the CFTC measures to substan-
26:980:74107:16:16:72:540:124:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:tiate a split of the sample of producingfirms intofirms that state they hedge, versusfirms that
26:981:74202:16:0:72:539:108:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:are self-stated non-hedgers. This split is then used as a robustness check for the futures return
27:982:74301:0:17:72:539:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:forecasting regressions. The goal is to substantiate that our results arise from fundamental hedging
27:983:74401:17:16:72:540:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:demand rather than from any omitted variable in our empirical model that simultaneously drives
27:984:74495:16:17:72:313:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:defaults and the commodity futures risk premium.
27:985:74543:17:16:88:539:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:We split the producers into two groups based on whether a producer is a stated hedger or
27:986:74631:16:17:72:539:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:non-hedger, according to the data we gathered in Section3on individualfirms’ disclosures about
27:987:74725:17:16:72:540:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:their hedging policies.  If our model is correct, the forecasting power of default risk for futures
27:988:74824:16:16:72:540:592:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:risk premia should ariseonlyfor thosefirms that engage in hedging. To implement the split, we
27:989:74917:16:17:72:543:576:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:must implicitly extrapolate the behavior of the samplefirmsbackwardsintime. Thisisbecause
27:990:75006:17:16:72:540:559:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the EDGAR data only contains information back to 1998. Panel A of Table II identifies 20firms
27:991:75099:16:17:72:539:543:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:as stated non-hedgers and 146firms as stated hedgers. We construct aggregate Zmijewski-scores,
27:992:75193:17:16:72:425:526:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Naive EDF’s, and 3-year average returns based on these two sets offirms.
27:993:75265:16:17:88:540:510:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:One concern that arises in this context is that hedgingfirms tend to be quite a bit larger than
27:994:75360:17:16:72:540:493:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the non-hedgers. In particular, the average market value of the hedgers is $3,035 million versus
27:995:75456:16:17:72:545:477:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:only $313 million for stated non-hedgers.  Furthermore, the sample of hedgingfirmsislarger,
27:996:75547:17:16:72:540:460:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:which reduces the idiosyncratic noise in aggregate measures constructed for this group offirms. To
27:997:75645:16:16:72:540:444:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:facilitate comparisons that are not driven by these differences, we identify a matched sample of self-
27:998:75747:16:17:72:539:428:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:described hedging producerfirms, by removing thefirms with the largest market values until the
27:999:75841:17:16:72:539:411:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:average market value of the small hedgers is aboutthe same as for the non-hedgers ($373 million);
27:1000:75938:16:17:72:540:395:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the standard deviation of the market values is also then comparable to that of the non-hedgers.
27:1001:76033:17:16:72:534:378:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:There are 59firms in this matched sample, and we run our tests also using this matched sample.
27:1002:76127:16:17:88:539:362:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:To decrease the amount of noise in the proxy for fundamental hedging demand in these tests, we
27:1003:76221:17:16:72:540:345:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:here define a consolidated default risk variable as simply an equal weighted average of the Zmijewski-
27:1004:76323:16:16:72:539:329:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:score, the naive EDF and the negative of the 3-year lagged stock return, where each of these variables
27:1005:76425:16:17:72:540:313:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:have been normalized to have zero mean and unit variance. The resulting consolidated, aggregate
27:1006:76520:17:16:72:540:296:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:default risk measures is also normalized to have unit variance so the regression coefficients are
27:1007:76617:16:17:71:539:280:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:easy to interpret and compare to the previous results.18Panel A of Table7shows the results of
27:1008:76710:17:16:72:539:263:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:regressions pooled across commodities, with aggregate default risk measures based on hedger- as
27:1009:76805:16:30:72:299:247:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:well as non-hedgerfirms on the right-hand-side:
27:1010:76852:30:19:128:483:217:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f7:C:=1(_+_)

27:1014:77157:15:15:80:540:136:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:18Since we only have data on the naive EDF until 2003Q3, thefinal observations up until 2006Q4 are based on the

27:1017:77497:11:0:71:176:99:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:the volatility of the series.
28:1018:77528:0:17:72:540:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:default risk measure of hedging producers. Panel A of Table7shows that in all the regressions
28:1019:77621:17:16:72:540:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the sign of1is strongly positive, while the sign of2is negative (and in most cases significant).
28:1020:77719:16:17:71:540:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Inspecting the magnitude of the regression coefficients, the implied regression coefficient on the
28:1021:77817:17:16:72:539:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:non-hedgers’ default risk measure (1+2) is, as expected, close to zero. Thus, it is the default risk
28:1022:77919:16:17:71:539:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of those producers that hedge exposure, not default risk in general, that drives aggregate hedging
28:1023:78017:17:16:71:232:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:pressure as defined by the CFTC.
28:1024:78049:16:16:88:539:592:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Panel B of Table7considers the futures return forecasting regressions using the same cross-

28:1028:78359:19:30:211:539:510:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f3:A:+2_+ ++1(25)
28:1029:78410:30:16:72:539:480:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:The table confirms that the difference in the forecasting power is statistically significant.  The
