28:1032:78706:16:17:72:540:431:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:default risk is close to zero in these specifications, which indicates that it is the default risk offirms
28:1033:78812:17:32:72:539:414:121:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:B:that actually do hedge that matters for the futures risk premium, rather than default risk per se.19
28:1034:78912:32:23:72:255:382:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:5.7  Commodity Spot Returns
28:1035:78939:23:17:72:540:359:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:The model predicts a strong common component in spot and futures returns arising from the
28:1036:79028:17:16:72:539:342:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:producers’ fundamental hedging demand. Table8shows forecasting regressions of quarterly spot
28:1037:79120:16:17:72:539:326:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:returns on the baseline lagged default risk measures, analogous to the regressions in Table4for the
28:1038:79219:17:29:71:351:309:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:case of the futures returns. In particular, the regression is:
28:1039:79281:29:30:154:539:280:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f3:A:+1=+ ++1(26)
28:1040:79341:30:16:71:544:250:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:where the control variables are the same as before. The spot return is as definedinSection3,the
28:1041:79436:16:17:72:540:234:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:change in the price of the nearest to maturity contract relative to its previous value. Table8shows
28:1042:79535:17:16:72:540:217:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that there is a clear positive relation between default risk and spot returns on commodities. In
28:1043:79631:16:17:72:539:201:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:particular, all the default risk measures are significant at the5%level or better in the pooled re-
28:1044:79730:17:16:72:539:184:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:gressions. The regression coefficients are very close to those found in the futures returns forecasting
28:1045:79833:16:16:72:540:168:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:regressions, as predicted by the model — the common component in the expected futures and spot
28:1046:79927:16:15:80:540:152:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:19This result also shows that our matching approach provides a useful alternative to the classification schemes
28:1047:80038:15:11:71:539:137:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:normally employed in the literature, namely, the CFTC reported classification of futures market participants into
28:1048:80151:11:11:71:539:126:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:hedgers and speculators (see De Roon et. al.(2000)). Our approach also offers an alternative to identification schemes
28:1049:80269:11:11:71:540:115:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:based purely on the reported functions of commodityfirms such as producer, refiner, marketer or distributor (see
28:1050:80381:11:0:71:540:104:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:Ederington and Lee (2002) for evidence that such classifications are noisy measures offirms’ actual hedging activities).
29:1051:80503:0:17:72:539:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:returns are of a similar size. Unlike in the results for futures returns, however, the basis is highly
29:1052:80605:17:16:72:539:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:significant in the pooled regressions. This is also consistent with the model, which predicts that
29:1053:80703:16:32:72:510:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the basis will indeed be more informative about future spot prices than futures risk premia.
29:1054:80795:32:16:88:539:626:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f3:A:Link between futures risk premium and the spot price.In the model, a decrease in
29:1055:80875:16:17:72:540:610:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the futures risk premium leads to an increase in the spot price as producers are willing to hold
29:1056:80971:17:16:72:540:593:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:more inventory when the cost of hedging is lower. The spot regressions are consistent with this
29:1057:81066:16:17:72:539:577:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:result, asceterus paribus, an increase in the spot price leads to a lower expected spot return. To
29:1058:81164:17:16:72:539:560:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the extent that the massive increase in speculator demand for long commodity futures positions
29:1059:81258:16:17:72:540:544:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:over the recent years led to a decrease in the futures risk premium, we should expect to have seen
29:1060:81356:17:16:72:539:527:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:an increase in the spot price. This effect is due to the possibility for increased risk-sharing between
29:1061:81459:16:16:72:540:511:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:producers and speculators on account of the lower futures risk premium. Note that an increase in
29:1062:81555:16:17:72:540:495:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:spot prices can occur through this channel even if there are no other changes in the fundamentals
29:1063:81652:17:32:72:347:478:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:(production and demand) of the commodity spot market.
29:1064:81705:32:24:72:218:446:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:5.8  Speculator Activity
29:1065:81729:24:16:72:540:422:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Following Etula (2009) and Adrian and Shin (2009), we use the growth in intermediaries’ (aggregate
29:1066:81827:16:16:72:539:406:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Broker-Dealer) assets relative to household asset growth as a measure of speculators’ ease of access
29:1067:81927:16:17:72:540:390:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:to capital in aggregate (−1). This data is constructed from the U.S. Flow of Funds data. Etula
29:1068:82023:17:16:72:540:373:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:(2009) shows that high relative growth in Broker-Dealer asset predicts low subsequent commodity
29:1069:82118:16:17:72:540:357:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:futures returns, consistent with a relaxation of capital constraints leading to a lower commodity
29:1070:82215:17:16:72:540:340:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:futures risk premium. The Broker-Dealer data is available quarterly for the full sample period. In
29:1071:82313:16:17:72:540:324:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:addition to this aggregate measure, we use the growth in Commodity Trading Advisors’ (CTAs)
29:1072:82404:17:16:72:540:307:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:aggregate assets-under-management (AUM) relative to aggregate household asset growth as a com-
29:1073:82498:16:17:72:539:291:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:modity specific measure of arbitrage capital. The CTA data is from a consolidated dataset, drawn
29:1074:82594:17:16:72:539:274:121:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:B:from HFR, TASS and CISDM databases, and is available from 1994 until the end of the sample.20
29:1075:82687:16:16:88:539:258:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Table9shows the results of forecasting regressions of the futures return, the spot return, and
29:1076:82781:16:17:71:540:242:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:annual inventory (the inventory is annual to nullify the effect of seasonalities). In addition to the
29:1077:82882:17:16:71:540:225:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:default risk measures used previously (the Zmijewski-score, the naive EDF and the 3-year stock
29:1078:82976:16:17:71:539:209:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:return), we add either the Broker-Dealer or the CTA measure of arbitrage activity as an independent
29:1079:83075:17:16:71:539:192:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:variable. The control variables used are the same as elsewhere in the paper. The table shows that
29:1080:83172:16:17:71:539:176:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the predictions of the model, listed in Proposition1are borne out in the data: expected spot
29:1081:83265:17:16:71:539:159:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and futures returns are (1) decreasing in speculator risk appetite, as proxied by speculator relative
29:1082:83366:16:17:71:539:143:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:asset growth, (2) increasing in producer hedging demand, and (3) the signs are the opposite when
29:1083:83462:17:14:80:539:126:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:20The panel of dollar AUM data is winsorized at the 0.25 and 99.75 percentile points and then aggregated across
29:1084:83573:14:11:71:539:112:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:all funds in specific self-declared strategies each quarter. These strategies are ’CPO-Multi Strategy’, ’CTA - Com-
29:1085:83688:11:0:71:421:101:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:modities’, ’CTA-Systematic/Trend-Following’, ’Managed Futures’ and ’Sector Energy’.
30:1086:83773:0:17:72:540:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f9:B:inventory holdings are the dependent variable. All the signs are as predicted and only3out of36
30:1087:83868:17:16:72:540:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:regression coefficients are statistically insignificant. The regression also shows that real quantities
30:1088:83971:16:17:72:539:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:(in this case inventory) are affected by limits to arbitrage and hedging demand, as predicted by the
30:1089:84071:17:31:72:104:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:model.
30:1090:84077:31:17:88:539:610:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f3:A:The interaction of speculator activity and producer hedging demand.In the dis-
30:1091:84155:17:16:72:539:593:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:cussion of Figure1, which shows the predictions of the calibrated model, we noted that the model
30:1092:84251:16:17:72:540:577:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:predicts an intuitive interaction between the severity of the speculator constraint and producers’
30:1093:84349:17:16:72:540:560:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:fundamental hedging demand. In particular, if speculators have ample capital, they are willing to
30:1094:84446:16:17:72:540:544:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:cheaply take the opposite side of producers’ hedge-motivated futures demand, while if speculator
30:1095:84542:17:16:72:453:527:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:capital is scarce, the compensation required (the futures risk premium) is large.
30:1096:84623:16:16:88:539:511:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:To empirically evaluate this interaction, we check whether the component of the Crude Oil
30:1097:84712:16:17:72:540:495:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:futures risk premium that is due to hedging pressure is negatively correlated with speculator relative
30:1098:84814:17:16:72:539:478:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:asset growth. The proxy for the fundamental hedging demand used here is the consolidated default
30:1099:84910:16:17:72:539:462:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:risk measure, based on a weighted average of the three default risk measures. The proportion of
30:1100:85005:17:16:71:539:445:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the risk premium due to producer hedging demand is constructed using the same regressions as
30:1101:85097:16:17:71:540:429:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:in Table4andEquation(21). In particular, the estimated risk premium due to producer hedging
30:1102:85188:17:13:71:540:412:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f9:B:demand (ˆ) is divided by the total estimated risk premium (ˆ+
30:1103:85281:13:20:73:539:399:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f3:B:ˆ), at each point in time. This measure is then squared to create a conditional
30:1104:85376:20:16:71:539:379:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f3:B:2, and we take the log of this measure to reduce itsskewness. While the regressions are quarterly,
30:1105:85475:16:16:72:540:363:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:we sum to an annual, overlapping quarterly series to avoid seasonalities and to better capture
30:1106:85569:16:17:72:540:347:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the underlying lower frequency dynamics.  The asset growth measures are also summed to an
30:1107:85658:17:16:72:540:330:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:annual, overlapping quarterly series. To avoid any systematic component in either of the series,
30:1108:85754:16:17:72:540:314:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the measures of arbitrageur asset growth and default risk are orthogonalized with respect to the
30:1109:85850:17:16:72:112:297:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:controls.
30:1110:85859:16:17:88:539:281:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Figure4shows the time-series of the speculator activity and producer hedging component of
30:1111:85948:17:16:72:540:264:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the risk premium over the sample period. Both variables are normalized to have zero mean and
30:1112:86040:16:16:72:540:248:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:unit variance for ease of comparison. The sample correlation and significance level is also shown
30:1113:86137:16:17:72:540:232:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:in the Figure. For the full sample using the Broker-Dealer measure (the top plot) the correlation
30:1114:86234:17:16:72:540:215:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:is -017and significant at the5%level.  That is, the proportion of the commodity futures risk
30:1115:86327:16:17:72:540:199:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:premium that is due to producer hedging demand tends to be low when arbitrage capital is high
30:1116:86420:17:16:72:539:182:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f9:B:and high when arbitrage capital is low, as predicted by the model. The middle plot on Figure4
30:1117:86513:16:17:72:540:166:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f9:B:showsthatthisrelationisstrongerinthelast12years of the sample. Here the correlation is -042
30:1118:86605:17:16:72:540:149:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and significant at the1%level. For the CTA data, which goes from 1994 to 2006, the full sample
30:1119:86699:16:16:72:539:133:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:relation is insignificant, although slightly positive, while the relation is strongly negative (-036)
30:1120:86801:16:17:72:540:117:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and significant at the5%level from 2000 until the end of the sample, when theflows of speculator
30:1121:86897:17:0:72:408:100:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:capital to the commodity markets were particularly large and volatile.
31:1122:86969:0:17:88:539:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:In sum, the evidence presented here indicates that time-varying market segmentation, due to
31:1123:87060:17:16:71:539:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:time-variation in the severity of limits to arbitrage for speculators in the commodity market, impacts
31:1124:87162:16:17:71:540:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:futures and spot commodity prices and inventories, through the hedging demand of producingfirms.
31:1125:87258:17:16:71:539:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:In particular, there is an intuitive, lower frequency interaction between speculator capital and the
31:1126:87358:16:17:71:539:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:impact of producer hedging demand and market prices that is uncovered when we consider annual
31:1127:87451:17:31:71:355:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:measures of hedging demand and speculator capital supply.
31:1128:87508:31:24:71:240:577:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:C:5.8.1  Other Robustness Tests
31:1129:87537:24:16:71:539:553:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:When splitting the sample, all the pooled regression coefficients indicate a positive relation between
31:1130:87639:16:17:71:543:537:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:producer fundamental hedging demand and the futures risk premium in thefirsthalfofthesample.
31:1131:87731:17:16:71:539:520:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:However, this effect is only statistically significant for the 3 year lagged return measure.  The
31:1132:87828:16:17:71:540:504:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:predictability evidence is stronger in the second half of the sample. Here all the pooled regressions
31:1133:87929:17:16:71:540:487:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:are significant at the 1% level or better. The magnitude of the regression coefficients are, however,
31:1134:88030:16:16:71:540:471:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:comparable across the samples.  We also considered the following additional controls: Surprise
31:1135:88124:16:17:71:540:455:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:OPEC production to control for international supply shocks, and aggregate Zmijewski-score of
31:1136:88216:17:16:71:539:438:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:airlines - the latter as a measure of hedging demand offirms that are consumers of the commodity.
31:1137:88313:16:38:71:515:422:121:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:B:None of these controls affect the economic or statistical significance of the reported results.21
31:1138:88410:38:28:72:189:384:209:g_d0_f2:209:g_d0_f2:C:6Conclusion
31:1139:88421:28:16:72:540:356:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:We build a theoretical model in which the interaction between commodity producers who are
31:1140:88510:16:17:72:540:340:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:averse to pricefluctuations, and capital constrained speculators that invest in commodity markets
31:1141:88607:17:16:72:540:323:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:determines commodity spot prices and commodity futures risk premia in equilibrium.  Using a
31:1142:88698:16:16:72:539:307:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:theoretically and empirically motivated proxy for the fundamental hedging demand of commodity
31:1143:88791:16:17:72:540:291:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:producers - their default risk - and data from oil and gas markets, wefind evidence to support the
31:1144:88889:17:16:72:540:274:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:predictions of the model. Our main insight is that the hedging demand of producers is an important
31:1145:88987:16:17:72:540:258:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:channel through which trading in commodity futures markets can affect spot prices. This occurs in
31:1146:89084:17:16:72:540:241:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:our model because futures markets allow producers’ inventory holdings to better adjust to current
31:1147:89181:16:17:72:201:225:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and future demand shocks.
31:1148:89206:17:16:88:539:208:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Our model and results provide a useful lens through which to view an important debate about
31:1149:89297:16:16:72:540:192:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:recent gyrations in commodity prices. Between 2003 and June 2008, energy, base metals, and pre-
31:1150:89392:16:17:72:540:176:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:cious metals experienced price rises in excess of 100%. Over the same period, there was a huge
31:1151:89486:17:16:72:539:159:121:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:B:increase in the amount of capital committed to long positions in commodity futures contracts.22
31:1152:89581:16:11:80:361:143:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:A:21These results are not reported, but they are available upon request.
31:1153:89651:11:15:80:539:132:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:22In July 2008, pension funds and other large institutions were reportedly holding over $250 billion in commodity
31:1154:89764:15:11:71:539:117:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:futures (mostly invested through indices such as the S&P GSCI) compared to their $10 billion holding in 2000
31:1155:89872:11:0:71:195:106:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:(Financial Times, July 8 2008)
32:1156:89904:0:17:72:540:691:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:While these trends occurred concurrently, some market practitioners and economists vehemently
32:1157:89997:17:16:72:539:674:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:argued that the speculative investments offinancial players in the futures market have no direct
32:1158:90093:16:17:72:540:658:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:relationship with commodity spot prices. Other commentators (most notably, Michael Masters, a
32:1159:90186:17:16:72:539:641:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hedge-fund manager, and George Soros, who both testified to the US Congress) have blamed spec-
32:1160:90280:16:17:72:540:625:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:ulative activity for recent commodity price rises. A third group (one that includes former Federal
32:1161:90378:17:16:72:540:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Reserve Chairman Alan Greenspan) has taken an intermediate view — that commodity spot prices
32:1162:90470:16:16:72:540:592:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:are fundamentally driven by physical demand, but thatfinancial speculation has played some role
32:1163:90565:16:17:72:540:576:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:in recent price rises. This last set of commentators has also argued thatfinancial speculation is in
32:1164:90665:17:16:72:539:559:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:fact stabilizing, for some of the reasons we outline in the model: the long positions taken byfinan-
32:1165:90765:16:17:72:540:543:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:cial investors have enabled producers to take short hedging positions and hold larger inventories,
32:1166:90863:17:16:72:439:526:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:which increases current spot prices and should stabilize prices going forward.
32:1167:90941:16:17:88:539:510:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:In support of this last view, we agree with the chain of reasoning specified for the rise in spot
32:1168:91038:17:16:72:540:493:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:prices.  This is also consistent with the fallout of the sub-prime crisis in 2008, which increased
32:1169:91136:16:17:72:540:477:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:speculator risk-aversion and simultaneously raised producer default risk. This increased producer
32:1170:91233:17:16:72:540:460:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:hedging demand at the same time that it became costlier to hedge, causing inventories to eventually
32:1171:91332:16:16:72:539:444:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:fall and lowering spot prices.  We acknowledge that our theory, which is based on risk-sharing
32:1172:91426:16:17:72:539:428:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:between producers and speculators, is unlikely to explain the fullmagnitudeof the rise and fall in
32:1173:91524:17:16:72:540:411:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:oil prices witnessed recently. Rather than a complete explanation, we view the mechanism we have
32:1174:91620:16:38:72:387:395:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:outlined as a likely contributing factor to recent price movements.
32:1175:91687:38:28:72:147:357:209:g_d0_f2:209:g_d0_f2:C:References

37:1310:101116:15:15:72:539:624:65:g_d0_f3:36:g_d0_f19:F:All moments are quarterly, corresponding to the empirical exercise in the next section. We calibrate the demand shock1

37:1312:101339:15:15:71:540:594:65:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:F:set the depreciation rate,,to001. Further, we assume the log stochastic discount factor (Λ) has a quarterly volatility of
37:1313:101462:15:15:71:544:579:65:g_d0_f11:65:g_d0_f3:F:20%and a mean of -025%, corresponding roughly to an annual equity Sharpe ratio of04and a risk-free rate of1%.Welet
37:1314:101578:15:15:71:539:564:65:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:F:the stochastic discount factor be perfectly negatively correlated with the demand shocks. Next, we calibrate the intratemporal

42:1777:112716:15:15:88:539:557:65:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:F:This analysis shows that the frictions assumed in this paper (limits to arbitrage and producer hedging demand) in general
42:1778:112837:15:15:72:539:542:65:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:F:equilibrium also affect the consumption of other goods and the equity market pricing kernel. Thus, the covariance term in
42:1779:112958:15:15:72:539:527:65:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:F:Equation (11)isaffected, not only through the volatility of the commodity price as in the partial equilibrium model in the
42:1780:113080:15:15:72:539:512:65:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:F:main text, but also through the dynamics of the pricing kernel (Λ). However, the identifying component of the frictions lies in
42:1781:113207:15:15:72:539:497:65:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:F:the risk compensation of the second term in Equation (11), which is related to the magnitude of desired hedging and the total
42:1782:113332:15:15:71:335:482:65:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:F:volatility (including any idiosyncratic components) of the futures price.
42:1783:113405:15:15:88:539:467:65:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:F:Since changes in producer and speculator variance aversion coefficients affect the pricing kernel, and thus the risk-free
42:1784:113526:15:15:71:540:452:65:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:F:rate (=1[Λ]−1), we cannot in general sign the effect of a change in these parameters on inventory and the futures
42:1785:113642:15:15:71:539:437:65:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:F:risk premium. In particular, in calibrated versions of the model, we for some parameter configurations obtain that inventory
42:1786:113766:15:15:71:539:422:65:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:F:decreases in response to an increase in producer fundamental hedging demand. However, the implications for the futures risk
42:1787:113889:15:0:71:433:407:65:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:F:premium remained robust in these calibrations (results not reported, but available upon request).

52:2216:141478:14:14:76:523:665:127:Times:127:Times:C:All plots have producer fundamental hedging demand (Jp{2,4,...,20}) on the horizontal axis. The 
52:2217:141575:14:14:76:532:651:127:Times:127:Times:C:dashed line corresponds to high speculator capital constraints (Js=40), while the solid line is the case 
52:2218:141680:14:13:76:500:637:127:Times:127:Times:C:of low speculator capital constraints ((Js=8)). The two top plots show the cost of hedging as a 
52:2219:141776:13:13:76:506:624:127:Times:127:Times:C:proportion of firm value (left) and the quarterly Sharpe ratio of the abnormal returns earned by 
52:2220:141873:13:13:76:529:611:127:Times:127:Times:C:speculators. The two middle plots show (on the left) the component of the futures risk premium due 
52:2221:141972:13:13:76:525:598:127:Times:127:Times:C:to the covariance with the equity market pricing kernel and (on the right) the component due to the 
52:2222:142072:13:13:76:524:585:127:Times:127:Times:C:combination of hedging pressure and limits to arbitrage. The two lowest graphs show the expected 
52:2223:142169:13:13:76:524:572:127:Times:127:Times:C:spot price change relative to the current spot price and the optimal inventory. The numbers used in 
52:2224:142269:13:13:76:377:559:127:Times:127:Times:C:the calibration of the model are given and explained in main text.
